Menachot 8 – The Flour Offering of the High Priest, in Halves
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhdK1exG4qFWlRZGM2SJ858z5ZqBYUuBrlLVb7LuFfc154xQPt6bQlyV1YWzMflpPx2tNodli21C-Yjz7v4A69jOplDwThNwhjcH3usNtYiw_enohQcLPoyje25FiAtwQ708FTYVbw7Nzo/s1600/George+Smith+of+Chichester+-+Still+Life+With+Bread+and+Cheese.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="255" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhdK1exG4qFWlRZGM2SJ858z5ZqBYUuBrlLVb7LuFfc154xQPt6bQlyV1YWzMflpPx2tNodli21C-Yjz7v4A69jOplDwThNwhjcH3usNtYiw_enohQcLPoyje25FiAtwQ708FTYVbw7Nzo/s320/George+Smith+of+Chichester+-+Still+Life+With+Bread+and+Cheese.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Every day the High Priest had to bring an offering made from an issaron (about 5 pounds) of flour. The dough was made into twelve loaves baked on a shallow pan, and he brought six in the morning and six in the afternoon. <br />
<br />
The Priest may want to place half of the flour in a vessel and sanctify it, then later do this for the other half. Regarding this, Rabbi Yochanan said that it cannot be sanctified in halves, but Rabbi Elazar allowed it.<br />
<br />
What is the reason of Rabbi Yochanan? The verse “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/6-20.htm">flour offering... half of it</a>...” means, “bring the complete offering and then divide it in halves.” And what is the reason of Rabbi Elazar? - Since it is offered in halves, it can be sanctified in halves.&nbsp;</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;"><br />
</span><br />
<span style="font-size: medium;">What can Rabbi Elazar answer to the verse used by Rabbi Yochanan? He agrees that it is better to do everything at once, but if the Priest did it in halves, this is  also valid. But the Torah uses the word “statute,” which means to be observed precisely?! - The Priest brings the complete amount from his home, but then can divide it.<br />
<br />
Art: George Smith of Chichester - Still Life With Bread and Cheese<br />
</span>

---

### content/menachot/80.txt
<a id="src-00067"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/80.txt`

Menachot 80 – Accidental Thanksgiving
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiid2AYhOuYIR9txM9yLZ8-XV63m7Sc0shkQuyvZOyVIo5m5eKydzHxoIqiJ8wZdwKcfHz4pnEEc4hk8CXpbeA5bE_5XqnQRLOutBPCRGcqA3Uez4Hr3qTEemk2Of0_pJQGe8HaJjxCWAo/s1600/John+Frederick+Herring+Snr+-+A+Cow+And+Calf+In+A+Stall.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="330" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiid2AYhOuYIR9txM9yLZ8-XV63m7Sc0shkQuyvZOyVIo5m5eKydzHxoIqiJ8wZdwKcfHz4pnEEc4hk8CXpbeA5bE_5XqnQRLOutBPCRGcqA3Uez4Hr3qTEemk2Of0_pJQGe8HaJjxCWAo/s400/John+Frederick+Herring+Snr+-+A+Cow+And+Calf+In+A+Stall.jpg" width="400" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A thanksgiving offering can be either a male or a female animal. If the female thanksgiving animal gave birth, its offspring is automatically sanctified as another thanksgiving, like its mother. However, unlike its mother, it does not require the forty breads to come with it.<br />
<br />
Similarly, if one says “let this animal be a substitute for this thanksgiving offering,” he has done something that is not right – for <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/27-10.htm">substitutes are prohibited</a> – but his words take effect, and now both animals are thanksgiving offerings; however, the second one is brought without the breads. This rule is also true when his thanksgiving offering was lost, he designated another one instead, and then the first one was found.<br />
<br />
Why this rule? – The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/7-12.htm">Then he shall offer with the thanksgiving offering matzah loaves</a>...” to teach us that only the thanksgiving offering requires loaves, but neither its offspring, its replacement, or its substitute require loaves.<br />
<br />
John Frederick Herring Snr - A Cow And Calf In A Stall<br />
</span>

---

### content/menachot/81.txt
<a id="src-00068"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/81.txt`

Menachot 81 – Thanksgiving Offering from Tithe
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgroqPIt1lSiE_AlRapcLIFv3Bp6q35Sa2HtL9FYWZdYxInQGrDpkx_dCsubCXwyiPzchfo0TFIP3biKNOSmLrct5QJMlkhe4LFNhSNAnF4jBCXSka-s91IGqFloYcMWt-eOB3gHm6ENIQ/s1600/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Study+Of+A+Dead+Stag.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="231" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgroqPIt1lSiE_AlRapcLIFv3Bp6q35Sa2HtL9FYWZdYxInQGrDpkx_dCsubCXwyiPzchfo0TFIP3biKNOSmLrct5QJMlkhe4LFNhSNAnF4jBCXSka-s91IGqFloYcMWt-eOB3gHm6ENIQ/s320/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Study+Of+A+Dead+Stag.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one said, “Let this animal be an exchange for my thanksgiving,” both animals are now sanctified. If one of them dies, the other one cannot be brought: if the live one is the thanksgiving, it needs breads, and if it is the exchange, it does not need bread. The students throughout time made eight attempts to resolve this problem and find the way to bring the animal. At fourth attempt by Levy, Rabbi Yehudah the Prince remarked, “This one looks like he has no brains in his head,” which was perfectly in order, since the students deduced laws even from Rabbi Yehudah's tone of answers.<br />
<br />
If one promises to bring a thanksgiving offering, he should use the animal and the breads from regular supplies. If he says, “I will bring it from the regular supplies and the breads from tithe,” his first words takes effect, and he has to bring both from regular supplies. If he promises to bring both from tithe, he may do so, only he should not bring the wheat kernels of tithe, but rather use the tithe money.<br />
<br />
Art: Sir Edwin Henry Landseer - Study Of A Dead Stag</span>

---

### content/menachot/82.txt
<a id="src-00069"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/82.txt`

Menachot 82 – One Can't Use Tithe In Place of Regular Produce
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgznbkM6HK6dkhmKh3VPvFXzx_F9-t5kJaxdxPj0Xe0EO-LLOBVOc1RD0vo3lvaoWm8wEQHuELjbsdteobddDCt02Qa5cipCbs4X2bu5BDvuUuEnyb9WehXHIZNsmYUydi3NyV4_m-_q6M/s1600/Jehan+Georges+Vibert+-+An+Afternoon+Libation.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="209" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgznbkM6HK6dkhmKh3VPvFXzx_F9-t5kJaxdxPj0Xe0EO-LLOBVOc1RD0vo3lvaoWm8wEQHuELjbsdteobddDCt02Qa5cipCbs4X2bu5BDvuUuEnyb9WehXHIZNsmYUydi3NyV4_m-_q6M/s320/Jehan+Georges+Vibert+-+An+Afternoon+Libation.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">As we <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/05/menachot-81-thanksgiving-offering-from.html">learned before</a>, if one says, “I promise to bring a thanksgiving offering,” he may bring it only from regular unconsecrated funds, and not from tithe. Why is this? – The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/16-2.htm">You shall slaughter the passover offering to God, your Lord, flocks and cattle</a>.” However, this cannot be understood literally, because the passover offering can come only from lambs and goats, and not from cattle. Then what does the word “cattle” teach us? To compare every other offering to the passover one, and say that just as a passover offering is an obligatory sacrifice that can be brought only from your own regular funds, so too every obligatory offering may be brought only from regular funds, and not from tithe. <br />
<br />
When one promises to bring a thanksgiving or a peace offering, he creates an obligation, and every obligatory offering must be brought from his own funds. Even when in his obligation he specifies to bring the animal from tithe, still the libations must come from regular funds – because all tithe must be eaten, and libations are not eaten but are rather completely offered on the Altar.<br />
<br />
Art: Jehan Georges Vibert - An Afternoon Libation</span>

---

### content/menachot/83.txt
<a id="src-00070"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/83.txt`

Menachot 83 - Learning Possible from the Impossible
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2xue1GGRm9_tz2_LzyKuaL_nPa1qyDWIOe-FLWLnfHbLBnXB5IjLM_fLoeVUscZUO8Ah2Ro4L9_rQmunb5VajEqIFWykY385OQC4V1h-KNRFU9HsigAg4-NEObqKr4F1ZmYgtfjqiYE4/s1600/Dieric+the+Elder+Bouts+-+The+Feast+Of+The-Passover+1464-67.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2xue1GGRm9_tz2_LzyKuaL_nPa1qyDWIOe-FLWLnfHbLBnXB5IjLM_fLoeVUscZUO8Ah2Ro4L9_rQmunb5VajEqIFWykY385OQC4V1h-KNRFU9HsigAg4-NEObqKr4F1ZmYgtfjqiYE4/s320/Dieric+the+Elder+Bouts+-+The+Feast+Of+The-Passover+1464-67.jpg" width="244" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Previously we <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/05/menachot-82-one-cant-use-tithe-as.html">compared all sacrifices to the Passover offering</a>, which had to be brought from regular funds, and not from tithe, and then all sacrifices got the same law. But how do we know this about Passover in the first place?<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer says, “We had a Passover offering in Egypt, and we also had it throughout the generations. Just as the one in Egypt had to be brought from private funds – because the tithe could only be taken from produce grown in Israel, which was not yet available – so too for all generations, the Passover offering has to be brought from private funds.” Rabbi Akiba answered, “How can we learn possible from the impossible? In Egypt it was impossible to use tithe, and afterwards it was possible!”  What does Rabbi Eliezer have to say? - “Even though it is an impossibility, we can learn a great lesson from it, because the first Passover Seder was a model for all later ones to come.”<br />
<br />
Art: Dieric the Elder Bouts - The Feast Of The-Passover 1464-67</span>

---

### content/menachot/84.txt
<a id="src-00071"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/84.txt`

Menachot 84 – Where Did the Grain Come From
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhixEVxSwLqXWVpjfTRknyiTwAK-ouOReG9f4bHbFGJB2tUdLH4yHGNWmYlswdb405vXbtl4fUpi_Rpg3X55Jk9zWJLgDA9j5YPiUyIbIevBOmjfN2G470tkz_bstXluyVWOZpa5A9g_Hk/s1600/John+Barrett+-+Gathering+the+Golden+Grain+near+Bishopsteignton%252C+Plymouth.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="184" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhixEVxSwLqXWVpjfTRknyiTwAK-ouOReG9f4bHbFGJB2tUdLH4yHGNWmYlswdb405vXbtl4fUpi_Rpg3X55Jk9zWJLgDA9j5YPiUyIbIevBOmjfN2G470tkz_bstXluyVWOZpa5A9g_Hk/s320/John+Barrett+-+Gathering+the+Golden+Grain+near+Bishopsteignton%252C+Plymouth.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">All flour offerings can be brought from any grain, whether from the new or old crop, grown in the Land of Israel or outside, except for the Omer, which is called “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/23-10.htm">the beginning of your harvest</a>” and the two loaves of Shavuot, which are called a “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/23-16.htm">new flour offering</a>,” for the last two have to be brought from the new crop, grown in the Land of Israel. <br />
<br />
All flour offerings must come from the choicest flour, as it says “<a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/12-11.htm">all the choice of your vows</a> – and which is the choicest? The villages of Machnis and Zitcha were the “alpha” of fine flour. Next in quality was the place called Aforaim, located in the valley (as opposed to another Aforaim in the mountains). All lands were therefore acceptable, but in practice they would only bring the grain from these.<br />
<br />
Art: John Barrett - Gathering the Golden Grain near Bishopsteignton, Plymouth</span>

---

### content/menachot/85.txt
<a id="src-00072"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/85.txt`

Menachot 85 – How to Grow the Best Grain
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggGKjSoXizaoRy41ZZYvx-UH-7GafRvL4-aMTZFXl2zNl4KuM6XqfRekVxY0IxMkra6m-72CHu5mv0O5-kjDQszSr1RrnAZVLxmzIlNoGnq91q_Zh8564BaRJ-NZ7XReqhzHX_W30zWno/s1600/Samuel+Bough+-+Sowing+the+Seed.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggGKjSoXizaoRy41ZZYvx-UH-7GafRvL4-aMTZFXl2zNl4KuM6XqfRekVxY0IxMkra6m-72CHu5mv0O5-kjDQszSr1RrnAZVLxmzIlNoGnq91q_Zh8564BaRJ-NZ7XReqhzHX_W30zWno/s320/Samuel+Bough+-+Sowing+the+Seed.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">For flour offerings, they would not use grain from fertilized fields, because once the field requires fertilization, perhaps it was not fertilized enough, or possibly because the use of fertilizer, which is malodorous, adversely affects the taste of the produce. They also did not use the grain from irrigated fields or from a field of trees, because it was not of the best quality. Such grain, though, would be acceptable after the fact.<br />
<br />
How then does one work the land to produce superior grain? He plows it the first year in the summer without sowing it in the winter. This gets rid of the thorns. Then in the second year he plows it again and now sows it, seventy days before Passover, and it produces abundant flour.<br />
<br />
How does one examine the flour? The Temple treasurer inserts his hand into it, and if dust comes up in his hand, the flour is invalid until he sifts it again. If the flour became wormy, it is permanently disqualified.<br />
<br />
Additional story - too much oil
<br /><br />
The Torah states, “He will dip his foot in oil” – that's talking about the land portion of Asher, where oil flows like a spring – because olive oil expands the mind.
<br /><br />
Once the people of Ludkiya needed oil. They appointed an agent to seek out the amount of oil bought for a million maneh, which equals to 400,000,000 golden dinars. The agent went to Jerusalem, this being the capital, but they told him to go to Tyre, which is a large port town. There, however, they directed him to Gush Chalav, in the portion of Asher.
<br /><br />
He came to Gush Chalav, and there they told him, “Go to so and so, to that certain field.” There he found a Jewish farmer, who was digging and hoeing under his olive trees. The agent asked, “Do you have the amount of oil for a million maneh?” - but the farmer replied, “Please wait till I finish my work.” After the farmer finished his work, he tied his tools and put them over his shoulder. As he was going, he was clearing away the stones from the field. The agent thought to himself, “Can such a hard-working man have that much oil? The Jews played a trick on me!”
<br /><br />
However, when the Jewish farmer reached his city, his maidservant brought out for him a small kettle of hot water, and he washed his hands and feet in it. Then she brought out for him a golden basin filled with oil, and he dipped his hands and feet in it, to fulfill literally the verse of “he dips his foot in oil.”
<br /><br />
After they ate and drank, the farmer measured out to the agent the million maneh's worth of oil, and then he said, “Do you need any more?” The agent said, “But I have no money left!” The farmer replied to him, “Take more, and I will come and collect the payment.” He measured out another 180 thousand maneh wroth of oil, and the agent had to rent every animal, horse, mule, camel, and donkey in Israel to transport the oil.
<br /><br />
The people of Ludkiya came to greet and praise their agent, but gave all honor to the farmer, who fulfilled the verse from king Solomon, “There is one who gives the impression of wealthy but has nothing, and there is one who gives the impression of being poor and has great wealth.”
<br /><br />
Art: Samuel Bough - Sowing the Seed</span>

---

### content/menachot/86.txt
<a id="src-00073"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/86.txt`

Menachot 86 – Which Oil?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiRrZHgHJCK_qdyuKmDowFYQmrkYY3mhCk222D-4WtsWwfkkha9KsADblR5DpDpXEsyg6i-LNQVVaDFdvrCNTDRCJ8G0kjFeIB_qvHkgMY1KWjw-EE71YG2y6SHNH2mtLuGm1i1vdsxD00/s1600/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+Olive+Trees+in+Bordighera.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiRrZHgHJCK_qdyuKmDowFYQmrkYY3mhCk222D-4WtsWwfkkha9KsADblR5DpDpXEsyg6i-LNQVVaDFdvrCNTDRCJ8G0kjFeIB_qvHkgMY1KWjw-EE71YG2y6SHNH2mtLuGm1i1vdsxD00/s320/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+Olive+Trees+in+Bordighera.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Oil had to be of superior quality. The city of Tekoa provided the “alpha” quality of oil, second to it was Regev from Trans-Jordan, and oil from other places was also valid. They &nbsp;avoided olives from fertilized or watered fields, or from fields where seeds were also grown. Oil from olives soaked in water, picked, or boiled was invalid. People of Tekoa were considered wise because they consumed oil regularly, and oil also led to great riches, as in the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/06/menachot-story-of-too-much-oil.html">story about a rich farmer</a>.<br />
<br />
Three times a year the olives are harvested, and in each harvest three grades of oil are extracted. For the first harvest one picks the crop from the top of the olive tree. He then pounds the olives in a mortar and puts them inside the basket. He then presses the olives with the beams to extract more oil. Finally, he grinds the olives with millstones and again presses them with a beam to extract yet more oil. The first oil is valid for the Menorah, and the other oils are valid for flour offerings. For the second crop he collects the olives from the rooftops of the nearby houses, and for the third one he collects the remaining olives in a vat.<br />
<br />
Art: Claude Oscar Monet - Olive Trees in Bordighera</span>

---

### content/menachot/87.txt
<a id="src-00074"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/87.txt`

Menachot 87 – Which Wine?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiSvyGoXaKc5yc8WquK_0CO994o-sRSRSkaD2PqSm0T6sByj-ABQ6MjYg0vEFiyd2AkQer4K_1D4NKqMN69nQbKwG8KRAfHAN57Fa6gJXyd9_BzQKW-eNXlx-GLUyRG5n1dD7Uj43NT4pc/s1600/Cornelis+van+Leemputten+-+A+Shepherd+with+Sheep+and+Lambs.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="197" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiSvyGoXaKc5yc8WquK_0CO994o-sRSRSkaD2PqSm0T6sByj-ABQ6MjYg0vEFiyd2AkQer4K_1D4NKqMN69nQbKwG8KRAfHAN57Fa6gJXyd9_BzQKW-eNXlx-GLUyRG5n1dD7Uj43NT4pc/s320/Cornelis+van+Leemputten+-+A+Shepherd+with+Sheep+and+Lambs.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The wine for libations – which had to be of the best quality – came from the places of Keduchim and Atulin, which produced the “alpha” quality, although wines from any place was valid.<br />
<br />
They avoided wines from fertilized fields, fields requiring irrigation, and fields where other seeds were also sown. Old, sweet, smoked, or cooked wines were invalid. Wine was not stored in large casks but in small barrel, and the barrel was not full, so that the aroma would spread when the barrel is opened.<br />
<br />
The best rams came from Moav, lambs from Hebron, calves from Sharon. Rabbi Yehudah says that the best lambs are those whose height is like their width. Rava bar Rav Shila explained this with the phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/isaiah/30-23.htm">your livestock will graze on that day, a broad lamb</a>.” He also said that God posted angels around the walls, whose task was to remind Him about Jerusalem. And what did these angels say before destruction? “<a href="http://bible.cc/psalms/132-13.htm">God chose Zion, desired it for His dwelling</a>.”<br />
<br />
There were two standard measures for flour in the Temple, “issaron” and half of “issaron,” for the standard flour offering and for the one of the High Priest.<br />
<br />
Art: Cornelis van Leemputten - A Shepherd with Sheep and Lambs</span>

---

### content/menachot/88.txt
<a id="src-00075"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/88.txt`

Menachot 88 – Seven Measures for Liquids
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_xXNd4jLspbXnaxF2voxgCSBDiMag0e2O8BKOU8eHfZ2WXzKP-ulbpwt45KXz_yE6M5bxQvnaL4mwkJtmz0WheQBC-Cehz-pcdWekpwllJI3_VoxzDWhC-DSR3c10Z0BYzthWXkzrh7Y/s1600/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+Water+Glass+and+Jug.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="253" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg_xXNd4jLspbXnaxF2voxgCSBDiMag0e2O8BKOU8eHfZ2WXzKP-ulbpwt45KXz_yE6M5bxQvnaL4mwkJtmz0WheQBC-Cehz-pcdWekpwllJI3_VoxzDWhC-DSR3c10Z0BYzthWXkzrh7Y/s320/Jean+Baptiste+Simeon+Chardin+-+Water+Glass+and+Jug.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There were seven types of measures for liquids in the Temple, based on a measure of “hin” (twelve login, or about 1 gallon): a hin, half-hin, third-of-a-hin, quarter-in, log, half-log, and a quarter-log. Rabbi Shimon says that the hin was not there, because only Moses used it, and then only once, but others claim that they kept Moses' hin. All that is based on the tradition that one needs seven liquid measures, and the measures have to be full. Rabbi Elazar bar Tzadok say that there was only one hin-measure, with incremental markings. He does not agree to the tradition of “seven measures.”<br />
<br />
What function did each measure serve? For example, the quarter-log was to measure the quarter-log of water for the purification of metzora (spiritual leper) and for the quarter-log of oil of a nazir.<br />
<br />
For all flour offerings the oil had to be measured with the “log” measure, so that an offering of sixty issaron (300 pounds) required to measure the log of oil sixty times. Rabbi Eliezer ben Yakov says that even a flour offering of sixty issaron would have only one log of oil in it.<br />
<br />
Art: Jean Baptiste Simeon Chardin - Water Glass and Jug</span>

---

### content/menachot/89.txt
<a id="src-00076"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/89.txt`

Menachot 89 – Mixing Libations
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUDRFHIgt6KOPy6t7YpzyN-ByteRYN4VMRJRWGk1p6WaDTBPDvkS60LaGfgKi3NRRFnv5D7pmi4Hqsp4WFM55A302PAayWc3bItQI2P4XPSY69mSMaUmKGINqZ2dEYWPYaHkGkTkxkTT0/s1600/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+A+Bull+And+Sheep+In+A+Landscape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUDRFHIgt6KOPy6t7YpzyN-ByteRYN4VMRJRWGk1p6WaDTBPDvkS60LaGfgKi3NRRFnv5D7pmi4Hqsp4WFM55A302PAayWc3bItQI2P4XPSY69mSMaUmKGINqZ2dEYWPYaHkGkTkxkTT0/s320/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+A+Bull+And+Sheep+In+A+Landscape.jpg" width="265" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Animal offerings were accompanied by libations, consisting of flour offering and wine. One may mix together the libations of bulls with the libations of rams, because they contain the same proportion of oil, that is, two logs (one cup) of oil per issaron (five pounds) of flour. <br />
<br />
The libations of lambs may be mixed with the libations of other lambs. These contain three logs (one-and-a-half cup) of oil per issaron of flour. One can even mix the libations of private individual's lamb with the libations of a communal lamb, and even those of today with those of tomorrow – as long as they did not get sanctified in a vessel.<br />
<br />
If one made the libations of bulls and accidentally mixed with the libations of lambs, they are valid, even though of different oil consistency – because they do not mix further. But if one mixed them before the ingredients were combined, the result is invalid.<br />
<br />
Art: Eugène Verboeckhoven - A Bull And Sheep In A Landscape</span>

---

### content/menachot/9.txt
<a id="src-00077"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/9.txt`

Menachot 9 – If Enemies Laid Siege to the Courtyard
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEie-lHQQ7T3bthn8l_HRRqWvvPziqgaQUVE99W7e78Go1QzIL3gktIKgFXoO8xC05Va2YkQkUYQggHNdg6YIxrvWr9kcCep6HFcAdrSdqBq4j6aoQtwMqVS7rflYHhGaaLNJtKrlK5Hb-A/s1600/Camille+Pissarro+-+The+Maidservant.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEie-lHQQ7T3bthn8l_HRRqWvvPziqgaQUVE99W7e78Go1QzIL3gktIKgFXoO8xC05Va2YkQkUYQggHNdg6YIxrvWr9kcCep6HFcAdrSdqBq4j6aoQtwMqVS7rflYHhGaaLNJtKrlK5Hb-A/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+The+Maidservant.jpg" width="247" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If enemies have surrounded the Courtyard of the Temple and are shooting into it, so that the Kohanim cannot eat sacrifices in the Courtyard, they are allowed to enter the Temple Hall and to continue eating the meat of the most holy offerings, as well as cooked flour-offerings, inside. How do we know that? The Torah says “<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/18-10.htm">in the most holy you shall eat it</a>” Most holy here means the Sanctuary, of the Temple Hall.<br />
<br />
But why would we need a verse to prove it? If offerings do not get disqualified in the Courtyard, which is subsidiary to the Hall, then of course they do not get disqualified in the Hall itself!? - That is true, they do not get disqualified, but for eating them we need a special permission. This is similar to a servant doing his work before his master, but to eat in the presence of his master – for that the servant needs a special permission. Therefore the verse teaches us that it is allowed.<br />
<br />
Art: Camille Pissarro - The Maidservant</span>

---

### content/menachot/90.txt
<a id="src-00078"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/90.txt`

Menachot 90 – Heaped Measures
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhq3gYU6F1IVKU-6wwKRZV8RPeU5KGXlYZXmg56ywFUrUyTib2LWrki4nkajShjM_kgnpR-8xVaxi4H3xhCQ5X_mwH7Y651DoWnPowdUs6Dm9jnB4d5MUPW3XsuidutBgTBiOeS4Ps4v0/s1600/Eastman+Johnson+-+Measurement+and+Contemplation+ca+1861-63.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="272" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhhq3gYU6F1IVKU-6wwKRZV8RPeU5KGXlYZXmg56ywFUrUyTib2LWrki4nkajShjM_kgnpR-8xVaxi4H3xhCQ5X_mwH7Y651DoWnPowdUs6Dm9jnB4d5MUPW3XsuidutBgTBiOeS4Ps4v0/s320/Eastman+Johnson+-+Measurement+and+Contemplation+ca+1861-63.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">All dry measures in the Temple were heaped, that is, to accomplish a proper measurement one had to fill the vessel and then heap flour on top. This follows the rule “there is no room for  poverty in the place of opulence.” The only exception to this was the daily flour offering of the High Priest, whose measure was leveled.<br />
<br />
Regarding liquid measures, their overbrim (liquid that rests above the level of the rim due to surface tension) is sacred, but the heap of dry measures is non-sacred. The teacher who composed this part of the ruling argues with the one who started it (also called the first teacher or tanna kama) about the sacredeness of the heap.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Akiba agrees that the liquid measures and their overbrim is sacred, but he argues about the dry ones and says that even the inside of the measure was not sanctified. Rabbi Yose says that the law of the overbrim is explained thus: liquids mix, and liquid top is as if it came from the inside, but dry measures do not mix.<br />
<br />
All sacrifices required libations, except for Passover, firstborn, and tithes, as well as sin offerings.<br />
<br />
Art: Eastman Johnson - Measurement and Contemplation ca 1861-63</span>

---

### content/menachot/91.txt
<a id="src-00079"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/91.txt`

Menachot 91 – Which Offerings Require Libations
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEa98ehJ0tbwobjH2EQwsWHmFhUJlLzbQ8nZkcaAHB9lENrzOSAZZCyPLqOipWRuqVDfrKMbHlLA7xaYkgqMQc3ZIjtaR1f_3cv9bMd3t_RharVzYNWpHfzKVNb9VlwEFt96iBastNcWk/s1600/James+Hayllar+-+Guilty+Or+Not+Guilty.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiEa98ehJ0tbwobjH2EQwsWHmFhUJlLzbQ8nZkcaAHB9lENrzOSAZZCyPLqOipWRuqVDfrKMbHlLA7xaYkgqMQc3ZIjtaR1f_3cv9bMd3t_RharVzYNWpHfzKVNb9VlwEFt96iBastNcWk/s320/James+Hayllar+-+Guilty+Or+Not+Guilty.jpg" width="236" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah said, “When you shall make a fire offering to God, burned offering, or another sacrifice.” I might have thought that any offering that goes on the fire requires libations, and even an offering of flour requires another flour libation with it. The prevent this, the Torah states “burned offering,” to exclude a flour offering. And how do I know that a peace offering requires libations? From the words “another sacrifice.” <br />
<br />
Among the sin-offerings, only the sin-offering of a metzorah (spiritual leper) and his guilt-offering require libations. How do I know that? The Torah stated, “the three-tenths of fine flour for a flour offering,” - and this is talking about an animal sacrifice of a metzorah. But perhaps he should bring a flour offering by itself? - Since the Torah later says “the kohen shall offer the burned offering and flour,” this leads me to understand that the Torah is speaking about the flour that comes with the animal offering.<br />
<br />
Art: James Hayllar - Guilty Or Not Guilty</span>

---

### content/menachot/92.txt
<a id="src-00080"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/92.txt`

Menachot 92 – Leaning on the Sacrifice
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUiAXSh7TsfEb0-zWcH-gYRB2-_zzO7Wvb3fvZsuC-2rqhC6A2POotDSBKqq9c2DSynSkFGXGzgyNBTLTA6DYu9qL21SDKeEP_rvv7nUfAzqudNrOb1EvB2Y0LQsE0_os8ki17NE-kUPM/s1600/Madame+Cezanne+Leaning+On+Her+Elbow.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUiAXSh7TsfEb0-zWcH-gYRB2-_zzO7Wvb3fvZsuC-2rqhC6A2POotDSBKqq9c2DSynSkFGXGzgyNBTLTA6DYu9qL21SDKeEP_rvv7nUfAzqudNrOb1EvB2Y0LQsE0_os8ki17NE-kUPM/s320/Madame+Cezanne+Leaning+On+Her+Elbow.jpg" width="264" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Most private offering required leaning, or “semichah,” when the owner of the sacrifice placed both his hands upon the sacrifice's head and pressed down with all his weight, before the sacrifice was slaughtered. If it was a sin-offering, he confessed his sin, and if it was a thanksgiving offering, he offered thanks to God. <br />
<br />
Communal offerings do not require leaning, except for the bull that comes for communal violations, and the he-goat dispatched to Azazel on Yom Kippur. Rabbi Shimon says that the he-goat for communal idolatry required leaning. There was a tradition that exactly two communal offerings required leaning, but they argued about which they were.<br />
<br />
All private offering required leaning, except for the first-born, tithe, and Passover offering. If one's father died and left a sacrifice, his son brings that sacrifice, performs leaning, brings the libations, and even has the power to appoint a replacement sacrifice. As we learned before, when one appoints a replacement, both animals become sacrifices, but to effect this, one needs to be a complete owner, and this teaches us that the son is a complete owner.<br />
<br />
Paul Cezanne - Madame Cezanne Leaning On Her Elbow</span>

---

### content/menachot/93.txt
<a id="src-00081"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/93.txt`

Menachot 93 – Who Has to Perform Leaning on the Sacrifices
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAiAHCTYT2kH4II2Seg60vrsPjbevpvcQTnGtT8MRCiQcxvo-gll2ztYhlAEHI1mfqNnYikE6wR_Lbw1E_9eDXYO0BpXC0ZJRKt5rl80yDlAMg3vejFHThfDUT1SR88pTY6dJxmEokkXY/s1600/Raphael+-+The+Mute+Woman.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhAiAHCTYT2kH4II2Seg60vrsPjbevpvcQTnGtT8MRCiQcxvo-gll2ztYhlAEHI1mfqNnYikE6wR_Lbw1E_9eDXYO0BpXC0ZJRKt5rl80yDlAMg3vejFHThfDUT1SR88pTY6dJxmEokkXY/s320/Raphael+-+The+Mute+Woman.jpg" width="232" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Basically, personal sacrifices require one to lean on them and recite either his guilt or his thanksgiving to God. However, there are some people who are exempt from this requirement. Thus, a deaf-mute, a deranged person, and a minor don't have the requirement of leaning, because they are not legally competent. In truth, since they cannot even consecrate an offering or bring it of their own free will, they are very rarely in a situation where leaning would be discussed.<br />
<br />
There are also categories of people who can bring a sacrifice without leaning altogether, and these include a non-Jew, a slave, an agent, and a woman. The agent of a person cannot perform leaning, because it says “your hand” - and not your agent's hand. A woman is not required to lean on her sacrifice because the Torah said “sons of Israel,” to exclude “daughters of Israel” from the requirement of leaning.<br />
<br />
Even if one is required to perform leaning and does not do it, the sacrifice is valid – although it is not done completely right. The leaning is done with both hands and is immediately followed with slaughter.<br />
<br />
Art: Raphael - The Mute Woman</span>

---

### content/menachot/94.txt
<a id="src-00082"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/94.txt`

Menachot 94 – The Twelve Breads of Vision
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhvVCqlJXuUPFb4KxwwToSHO9Z6cHHUB8l7LeQxPaB0DTc0JIGmM3Z0QcpbroCDDrJv6yIVe-AxaVkw3JvOWZu4EaCGuFGTv57L-1MfXy7Fu6LUxcao3RFwyql5w95iobTZNbXK3LMVro/s1600/Gustave+Caillebotte+-+Boater+Pulling+On+His+Perissoire.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="253" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhvVCqlJXuUPFb4KxwwToSHO9Z6cHHUB8l7LeQxPaB0DTc0JIGmM3Z0QcpbroCDDrJv6yIVe-AxaVkw3JvOWZu4EaCGuFGTv57L-1MfXy7Fu6LUxcao3RFwyql5w95iobTZNbXK3LMVro/s320/Gustave+Caillebotte+-+Boater+Pulling+On+His+Perissoire.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">In some aspects leaning on the sacrifice is stricter than waving it: if many partners bring a sacrifice, each one has to lean on it. But in some aspects waving is stricter than leaning: waving applies to the individual and community sacrifices, live or slaughtered ones, and it even applies to non-living matter, such as loaves.<br />
<br />
The two loaves on Shavuot were kneaded one by one and baked one by one, but the twelve breads of vision, brought every Shabbat, were kneaded one by one and baked in pairs. The reason for separate kneading is so that every loaf would get its correct amount of flour.<br />
<br />
The breads of vision were baked in a mold and then transferred to another golden mold. Baking in a mold was required because of the breads' special shape: according to Rabbi Chanina, they were shaped like an open box, and according to Rabbi Yochanan, they were shaped like a small fast boat dancing on the waves.<br />
<br />
Art: Gustave Caillebotte - Boater Pulling On His Perissoire</span>

---

### content/menachot/95.txt
<a id="src-00083"></a>

**Source file:** `content/menachot/95.txt`

Menachot 95 – Where Was the Bread of Vision Baked?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKJFz2qhYUltJWur31A_YkKlTZ-Vr0HSklikfiH0V17i4mwRGSscPYtwwLXBruFfShMaCS-5QrlY5szLYjQr3X3vtyvWJ2u1-cmKmO-cX-jMDEvxP3KiUjcoOVhs9yzKcleXQOFGX_i5c/s1600/Pieter+de+Hooch+-+A+Woman+Preparing+Bread+and+Butter+for+a+Boy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgKJFz2qhYUltJWur31A_YkKlTZ-Vr0HSklikfiH0V17i4mwRGSscPYtwwLXBruFfShMaCS-5QrlY5szLYjQr3X3vtyvWJ2u1-cmKmO-cX-jMDEvxP3KiUjcoOVhs9yzKcleXQOFGX_i5c/s320/Pieter+de+Hooch+-+A+Woman+Preparing+Bread+and+Butter+for+a+Boy.jpg" width="248" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When the Jews traveled in the desert, did the Bread of Vision become invalid at the beginning of each journey? Since the  the bread was moved from its place, is this  the same as leaving the curtains, or does the Tabernacle retain its status to protect the bread from invalidation?  Rabbi Yochanan and Rabbi Yehoshua ben Levi argue about this, but we do not know who held what view. Based on the phrase “<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/2-17.htm">as they encamp so shall they journey</a>,” the bread in travel becomes invalid just as in the encampment, but based on “<a href="http://bible.cc/numbers/4-7.htm">and the constant bread shall remain upon the table</a>,” the bread remains valid.<br />
<br />
The bread of vision was kneaded outside the Temple – because vessels did not sanctify the flour – and baked inside the Temple before Shabbat. Rabbi Yehudah disagrees: it was kneaded and baked inside the Temple, on Shabbat, to protect the bread from staying overnight. Rabbi Shimon maintains that both ways are valid. Their proofs are not based on the <a href="http://bible.cc/1_samuel/21-6.htm">story of King David and the priestly bread</a> – for David had a case of boulimia – extreme hunger – but on tradition.<br />
<br />
Art: Pieter de Hooch - A Woman Preparing Bread and Butter for a Boy</span>

---

Menachot 96 – Wafers of the High Priest
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2PWvqYJl5wyd6cOyAv64gfWEkiD6rkUSeX2lTuin5-Al6BdUUA2CQvw28BpOUsyDSiwzz3ZHbZQC9mrMYlKJW8x5ZetlPaVzb-90Q4k48RTy6YsTuTy9fECU_hsFUcb3URSSeFDUGkiw/s1600/Evaristo+Baschenis+-+Boy+With+A+Basket+Of+Bread.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="232" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi2PWvqYJl5wyd6cOyAv64gfWEkiD6rkUSeX2lTuin5-Al6BdUUA2CQvw28BpOUsyDSiwzz3ZHbZQC9mrMYlKJW8x5ZetlPaVzb-90Q4k48RTy6YsTuTy9fECU_hsFUcb3URSSeFDUGkiw/s320/Evaristo+Baschenis+-+Boy+With+A+Basket+Of+Bread.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Each day, the High Priest brought twelve wafers, six in the morning and six in the afternoon. In the morning he would bring and consecrate a full tenth (issaron, or 5-pound measure) of flour and divide it into two halves. Kneading and baking of the wafers was done daily, even on Shabbat, but grinding and sifting of their flour was done before. Rabbi Akiva formulated a rule: “Even when the Torah allowed a  labor on Shabbat, it allowed only that portion of it that could not be done before Shabbat.”<br />
<br />
The two loaves on Shavuot were seven hand-breadths long and four hand-breadths wide. They had strips of dough at the corners, or “horns,” that were four finger-breadths long. The breads of visions were larger: ten hand-breadths long, five hand-breadths wide, and their “horns” were seven finger-breadths in length.<br />
<br />
Ben Zoma explained that the “Bread of Vision” can also be translated as the “Bread of Faces,” meaning that it should have many “faces,” or surfaces, thus the complicated shape.<br />
<br />
Art: Evaristo Baschenis - Boy With A Basket Of Bread<br />
</span>

---

### content/menachot/97.txt
<a id="src-00085"></a>
