<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilTPgSC9lZ4oxZ1SpBxLpzTWQfDdw-mRzSyLFeXcrIp8Tbvuq-Zyluxof6GK6Tq5gF_96SVPup4Eju3SiJU332cjGr8zSpijOGopFzW3kWt76yZLMQXJVqKW2Sj9PnYkDsyZqEo6zxoouC/s1927/Draper-Pot_Pourri.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1443" data-original-width="1927" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEilTPgSC9lZ4oxZ1SpBxLpzTWQfDdw-mRzSyLFeXcrIp8Tbvuq-Zyluxof6GK6Tq5gF_96SVPup4Eju3SiJU332cjGr8zSpijOGopFzW3kWt76yZLMQXJVqKW2Sj9PnYkDsyZqEo6zxoouC/s320/Draper-Pot_Pourri.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>All the people who came to slaughter their Passover sacrifices were divided into three groups, one entering the Courtyard after another. Why three? - In the phrase "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1823" target="_blank">the entire <b>community</b>, <b>assembly</b> of <b>Israel</b></a>," each word indicates a group. The group comes in, the gates close, the Levites blow the trumpets. The Kohanim priests stood ready in rows. Some rows had all golden vessels and some - all silver.<p></p><p>The sacrifice owner would slaughter it (if he knew how), and a Kohen would receive the blood and pass it to the next Kohen in line. This continued until they reached the Kohen closest to the Altar, who would then throw the blood on the Altar's wall. Everybody sang the Hallel. If they had to, they would repeat it, but Kohanim were fast, and they seldom had to repeat the Hallel, and definitely not sing it the third time.</p><p>There were hooks on which they could suspend and flay the offerings. For those for whom there was not a hook, there were planks of wood. One could set the plank on his and his friend's shoulder and flay it.</p><p>Three groups of people were a requirement, but the third was called "the lazy group." This agrees with Rabbi Yehudah's philosophy that "The world needs perfume makers and leather makers (which is associated with bad odor). But one should strive to be among perfume makers."</p><p>Art: Potpourri by Herbert James Draper</p>

---

### content/pesachim/65.txt
<a id="src-00425"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/65.txt`

Pesachim 65 - Passover sacrifice blood on the Temple floor
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjcfHIRvuRJ42UW98Q6zX-e6xXeyXZK4cA4Nu6GZTMLDKOkdWv8gOW_42rcKLZBAqhcaBw1BPTeWAR0JwvygDxqbMubhCESfilowZ8WN1bifuwlYegqE57WBfYSVXJCK9QlQq1N-asgls4k/s1200/1200px-Gustave_Caillebotte_-_The_Floor_Planers_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" style="clear: left; display: inline; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="843" data-original-width="1200" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjcfHIRvuRJ42UW98Q6zX-e6xXeyXZK4cA4Nu6GZTMLDKOkdWv8gOW_42rcKLZBAqhcaBw1BPTeWAR0JwvygDxqbMubhCESfilowZ8WN1bifuwlYegqE57WBfYSVXJCK9QlQq1N-asgls4k/s320/1200px-Gustave_Caillebotte_-_The_Floor_Planers_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>If the time to bring the Passover sacrifice fell on Shabbat, it proceeded as on weekdays - because the Torah said to bring it at "its appointed time" - even on Shabbat. The Kohanim priests would even wash the floor on Shabbat, but here the Sages disagreed with them - because washing the floor wasn't for the sacrifice's needs.<p></p><p>Since some blood would inevitably spill on the Courtyard's floor, Rabbi Yehudah recommended scooping a cup from the floor and throwing it on the Altar walls. Otherwise, that sacrifice for which the blood spilled would be invalid. The Sages disagreed because the minor amount of blood that spilled would be nullified in all other blood. Rabbi Yehudah answered that like does not get nullified in like.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;&nbsp;The Floor Scrapers by Gustave Caillebotte</p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/66.txt
<a id="src-00426"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/66.txt`

Pesachim 66 - How Rabbi Akiva has set up Rabbi Eliezer
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUEc6re536sHFZPyr8dMY4q6dPlE0-R0FDtOUrTiFRlZept6Ozz3RJgUWJE3iIY0aaIN33cqOG_ty5Uop-fJdH3bPq-CIew9XJ2tvc89cdfoIsiSXuyBukeeuve0JFgpbdgXzc-cZ9WzM7/s600/Pietro_Longhi_-_Vendor_of_Roast_Meat_-_WGA13420.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="446" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUEc6re536sHFZPyr8dMY4q6dPlE0-R0FDtOUrTiFRlZept6Ozz3RJgUWJE3iIY0aaIN33cqOG_ty5Uop-fJdH3bPq-CIew9XJ2tvc89cdfoIsiSXuyBukeeuve0JFgpbdgXzc-cZ9WzM7/s320/Pietro_Longhi_-_Vendor_of_Roast_Meat_-_WGA13420.jpg" /></a></div>When Passover eve - time to bring the Passover sacrifice - falls out on Shabbat, it is still permitted to bring this sacrifice even if this violates Shabbat laws. One can do the slaughter, throw the blood on the Altar walls, and remove the intestines and the waste. However, roasting the meat can and should be done after Shabbat.<p></p><p>Likewise, such acts as carrying the sacrifice on one's shoulders to the Temple or bringing it from afar do not override Shabbat rules. Here Rabbi Eliezer disagrees and says that they do override Shabbat because, in his view, the love of the mitzvot tells us to violate Shabbat in preparing for a mitzvah that will be done on Shabbat.</p><p>As Rabbi Eliezer got carried away defending his position, Rabbi Akiva prepared a trap for him. He constructed a logical argument that seemed to uproot the teachings of the Torah. He said, "Look at the mitzvah of purifying one for the Passover - it did not become permitted on Shabbat even though it was needed! So, Rabbi Eliezer, don't be surprised that the Torah did not allow the Passover sacrifice to be brought on Shabbat."</p><p>Rabbi Eliezer fell for it and exclaimed, "Akiva! You are ruining what the Torah said! It told us to bring the sacrifice<b>&nbsp;at the appointed time</b>!" Now Rabbi Akiva countered, "Please show me where the Torah says <b>the appointed time</b> for those other acts that you allow."</p><p>Art: Vendor of Roast Meat by&nbsp; Pietro Longhi&nbsp;</p>

---

### content/pesachim/67.txt
<a id="src-00427"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/67.txt`

Pesachim 67 - Pesach sheni and community that is not pure
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjCG13GBh1uCe7Sja4jDegJYfjsQjPA5j5K_IDPTAFY85HAgV6joWMrpKs8seAlSF43SRqRXMcnrVqY3_o44sBKQazcNlltUan9abcvwNi8WqxXxs6oKtPVsVZwOmmDreydVEz7BKr6Jl57/s1029/Death_of_Marat_by_David.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1029" data-original-width="800" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjCG13GBh1uCe7Sja4jDegJYfjsQjPA5j5K_IDPTAFY85HAgV6joWMrpKs8seAlSF43SRqRXMcnrVqY3_o44sBKQazcNlltUan9abcvwNi8WqxXxs6oKtPVsVZwOmmDreydVEz7BKr6Jl57/s320/Death_of_Marat_by_David.jpg" /></a></div>If one is not pure with the dead's impurity and does not have the time to purify himself - since this requires seven days - he will be celebrating a repeat, called Pesach Sheni, a month later. However, if the whole community is not pure, then the Passover offering is brought nevertheless. Where is this in the Torah?<p></p><p>It said, "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=9#P3973" target="_blank">Any person who would be impure from a corpse</a>...celebrates it a month later". This tells us that any individual is barred from bringing the sacrifice, but the community is not. That was the suggestion of Rabbi Yochanan. However, his student, colleague, and constant opponent Resh Lakish suggested that it could mean the following: an individual has a way out by celebrating Pesach Sheni, but a community has no way out at all. The Talmud goes through a string of proofs and confirms our rule.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;&nbsp;The Death of Marat by Jacques-Louis David</p>

---

### content/pesachim/68.txt
<a id="src-00428"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/68.txt`

Pesachim 68 - Where is the resurrection of the dead in the Torah?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_hbf6bip8l-ksfJuQg3JxAsW_2LQRmcVlq8TYACZRujze9KloUWmVEVATkQtAeG_KPWac904gZZOChrg-bjAuNtD8R1y3co8OZh90VyaAKXUIfX504vgNijXdMj63U3khBierNrhFghjT/s781/781px-Sebastiano_Ricci_-_St_Anthony_of_Padua_Healing_a_Youth_-_WGA19414.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="599" data-original-width="781" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj_hbf6bip8l-ksfJuQg3JxAsW_2LQRmcVlq8TYACZRujze9KloUWmVEVATkQtAeG_KPWac904gZZOChrg-bjAuNtD8R1y3co8OZh90VyaAKXUIfX504vgNijXdMj63U3khBierNrhFghjT/s320/781px-Sebastiano_Ricci_-_St_Anthony_of_Padua_Healing_a_Youth_-_WGA19414.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>It says in the Torah, "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=32#P5792" target="_blank">I put to death and I make live</a>,"&nbsp; and it continues, "I have wounded, and I will heal." You could say that some people die while some other people come alive. However, just as healing only applies to the person who had been previously wounded, so too, life applies to that one who had previously died. Incidentally, we also see the order of the events: at first, "what I had put to death, I will make live," and then - "what I have wounded, I will heal." Who will be doing the resurrection? - It's the righteous, with their staffs, hinting at the staff of Elisha who "placed it on the face of the boy."<p></p><p>The page also deals with removing a wart, which represents a temporary blemish on the Passover sacrifice.</p><p>Art: St Anthony of Padua Healing a Youth by Sebastiano Ricci&nbsp;</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/69.txt
<a id="src-00429"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/69.txt`

Pesachim 69 - More meat for the Seder
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMhSerKijOwmdGOB9B966EfGBeygMJJSlBMmF0R9x_5Y6k9c_3iBTgNA2mxxzkDlC8mz3HNPqVX53eyO4oYfDOi5y4prVOl_SP0rTI-LYAlKq-xGNuG8q9F_L4iVZGDa7rs42BMvwX4kgB/s736/736px-Philipp_Peter_Roos_-_Italianate_Landscape_with_a_Goat_and_Sheep_-_WGA20036.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="736" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMhSerKijOwmdGOB9B966EfGBeygMJJSlBMmF0R9x_5Y6k9c_3iBTgNA2mxxzkDlC8mz3HNPqVX53eyO4oYfDOi5y4prVOl_SP0rTI-LYAlKq-xGNuG8q9F_L4iVZGDa7rs42BMvwX4kgB/s320/736px-Philipp_Peter_Roos_-_Italianate_Landscape_with_a_Goat_and_Sheep_-_WGA20036.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Since the Passover offering should be eaten in a kingly manner - in abundance and not in hunger - another offering to provide more meat was often brought. This other offering is called "chagigah," or the festival offering.&nbsp;<p></p><p>However, this chagigah had more conditions attached to it than the Passover offering. The chagigah was brought only on the Passover that fell on a weekday, not on Shabbat. Chagigah was also not brought when there was enough of the Passover lamb anyway, such as few invitees in the group.</p><p>The chagigah could be a sheep, a cow, a goat, male or female, and, unlike Passover, it could be eaten for two days and one night.</p><p>Art: Landscape with a Goat and Sheep by Philipp Peter Roos</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/7.txt
<a id="src-00430"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/7.txt`

Pesachim 7 – Right after searching for chametz…
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhaw24Xr-KvwVU9QDGAz0rlX5qgCZGX5kve94iMeI_W3IBWuMF4PVtLcnLFaP8BC4U8zyaWz4NM2Id2BGlvoAIbpEJ00bf0VKJzysTz5akH7-hVrW1qJ0lCDbniC1Jn5Ng_39Us95mpSM_5/s600/Searching.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="243" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhaw24Xr-KvwVU9QDGAz0rlX5qgCZGX5kve94iMeI_W3IBWuMF4PVtLcnLFaP8BC4U8zyaWz4NM2Id2BGlvoAIbpEJ00bf0VKJzysTz5akH7-hVrW1qJ0lCDbniC1Jn5Ng_39Us95mpSM_5/s320/Searching.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
After one finishes <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/06/pesachim-4-why-search-for-chametz-so.html">searching for and destroying his chametz</a>, he must also declare whatever he missed as ownerless, the dust of the earth, and not belonging to him. Why is that? He just destroyed all his chametz anyway!?
<br />
<br />
One reason is that he might find a nice loaf of bread later. Since it is nice, he will desire it and in his mind own it, at least for a few seconds, and thus transgress the prohibition of owning chametz. Declaring it ownerless helps.
<br />
<br />
Still, why does he need to declare the chametz that is unknown to him ownerless? He might as well say this declaration the minute he sees the bread!? – By the time Pesach comes, it is not in his power to declare it ownerless. 
<br />
<br />
Here we have an interesting paradox, as Rabbi Elazar puts it. There are two things that are not in the possession of a man, yet the Torah holds him responsible as if they were his. The first one is a pit in the street. If one opens it, then even though it does not belong to him, he still pays for the damages caused by the pit. The second one is chametz on Pesach: even though one cannot use it for any purpose or derive benefit from it (so technically it does not belong to him,) the Torah still considers it as if he transgressed “No leaven should be found with you on Passover” when it is found in his domain.
<br />
<br />
Art: Searching by Valentin Walter Bromley (1848-1877)

---

### content/pesachim/70.txt
<a id="src-00431"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/70.txt`

Pesachim 70 - What is the difference between a knife and a cleaver
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHzvMyrRaxCeUeTjXBsfbxDEQLIh4fAE6nFCMZ3fFpIqgpqWvGsnVjp_bX3re2dqNxHVlL_n3izW7_KiqBXaikE3y3BXPcfb4WubEwUfoJcfSzxXnA7soUEygvxNq2zD6CsD_CYYfPEbi6/s880/3d3f089d-smush-fleisch4.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="880" data-original-width="660" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHzvMyrRaxCeUeTjXBsfbxDEQLIh4fAE6nFCMZ3fFpIqgpqWvGsnVjp_bX3re2dqNxHVlL_n3izW7_KiqBXaikE3y3BXPcfb4WubEwUfoJcfSzxXnA7soUEygvxNq2zD6CsD_CYYfPEbi6/s320/3d3f089d-smush-fleisch4.jpg" /></a></div>On the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/01/pesachim-69.html" target="_blank">previous page</a>, we said that the Festival offering called Chagigah is different from the Passover offering: it is eaten for two days and a night in between, it can be boiled and not roasted, and so on. However, Ben Beteira thinks differently and holds that it is exactly the same as Passover offering in most respects. Even though Ben Beteira's view does not become the accepted law, the Talmud spends significant effort investigating what Ben Beteira thinks about various aspects of Passover.<p></p><p>An even more special situation is found in the next rule that talks about finding a knife and a cleaver right before Passover. The knife is for the Passover offering where, by the way, the bones are not allowed to be broken. The cleaver is for Chagigah, the Festival offering, where there is no such prohibition. But the only situation when the two will be treated the same is when the community was pure on the day before Passover and suddenly became impure the next day. And the only situation where <i>that</i> can happen is when the head of the Sanhedrin, de-facto spiritual ruler, was on the verge of death before Passover. The community was all pure, but there was an all-too-real possibility that they will all go to his funeral the next day and thus become impure. The Talmud does not comment if this combination of events ever occurred in history.</p><p>Art: Carcass of Beef by Rembrandt</p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/71.txt
<a id="src-00432"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/71.txt`

Pesachim 71 - Trying to do a mitzvah but failing
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgP__hNRYepFRW4r6Qdy5_-UtjdL6c5o8t8kOMFt1sEn2tpXNt2MDFudPI55FfvVus5Yw0YeDkhGAkjvbpPgY2ldqWYtVXIEHLa61paMlBkoly6CDP_zmtnUy6nQoj4kA-nkcUdQec7vHR5/s1280/1280px-A_Meat_Stall_with_the_Holy_Family_Giving_Alms_-_Pieter_Aertsen_-_Google_Cultural_Institute.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="891" data-original-width="1280" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgP__hNRYepFRW4r6Qdy5_-UtjdL6c5o8t8kOMFt1sEn2tpXNt2MDFudPI55FfvVus5Yw0YeDkhGAkjvbpPgY2ldqWYtVXIEHLa61paMlBkoly6CDP_zmtnUy6nQoj4kA-nkcUdQec7vHR5/s320/1280px-A_Meat_Stall_with_the_Holy_Family_Giving_Alms_-_Pieter_Aertsen_-_Google_Cultural_Institute.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>One should slaughter a Passover lamb on the Passover day, even if it falls out on Shabbat - when the slaughter is usually forbidden. However, if his slaughter is invalid, he has transgressed Shabbat, albeit retroactively, and now he needs to atone for it by bringing a sin-offering after the Holidays. For example, this happens when he takes a Passover offering and brings it for the sake of peace offering, which makes it completely invalid.<p></p><p>However, if he takes a peace offering and slaughters it as Passover, he has done at least some sort of a mitzvah, and Rabbi Yehoshua says that he does not need to bring a sin-offering.&nbsp;</p><p>If the animal had a blemish (which invalidates any offering), he should have checked it before the slaughter. That is negligence, and even Rabbi Yehoshua says that he is liable to a sin-offering. But if it is invalid due to an animal's internal defect, then everybody agrees that there is no sin-offering because it was like an unavoidable accident. The meat is not kosher and cannot be eaten, but he is not to blame.</p><p>Art: Butcher’s Stall by Pieter Aertsen</p>

---

### content/pesachim/72.txt
<a id="src-00433"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/72.txt`

Pesachim 72 - Circumcision and Passover on Shabbat - what's the difference?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiAzqvwEfio6GOTE-t13jRFuUFjDiKsrd6sLRyeSEdhrLWKFgi5P6a14AIOuq3wwNtNakNtDUuxtnyuEPpBLeABrv5BcxsIx5cyM9H_GR5akbDLFW0JVTVnfbBX2JQX4Lw8eARW6ZaOmE1r/s977/977px-Rubens_Two_Sleeping_Children.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="768" data-original-width="977" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiAzqvwEfio6GOTE-t13jRFuUFjDiKsrd6sLRyeSEdhrLWKFgi5P6a14AIOuq3wwNtNakNtDUuxtnyuEPpBLeABrv5BcxsIx5cyM9H_GR5akbDLFW0JVTVnfbBX2JQX4Lw8eARW6ZaOmE1r/s320/977px-Rubens_Two_Sleeping_Children.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Similar to the Passover sacrifice, if the circumcision day (eighth after birth) occurs on Shabbat, the circumcision is performed even though by doing it, one creates a wound.&nbsp;<p></p><p>Let's say one had two babies that he needed to circumcise, one on Friday and the other one on Shabbat. He messed up and circumcised the Friday baby on Shabbat. He violated Shabbat but did the mitzvah. You can say that he was negligent. So why does Rabbi Yehoshua exempt him here but obligates him in a sin-offering in&nbsp;the Passover offering&nbsp;case&nbsp;that we <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/01/pesachim-71-trying-to-do-mitzvah-but.html" target="_blank">saw earlier</a>?</p><p>The answer is in the additional details. First, he circumcised the Friday baby. So he was still preoccupied with the remaining Shabbat baby. This explains his error and exempts him from the sin-offering. In the case of Passover, he already did the mitzvah the wrong way and had no other mitzvah to distract him, so there Rabbi Yehoshua makes him liable.</p><p>Art: Two Sleeping Children by Peter Paul Rubens</p>

---

### content/pesachim/73.txt
<a id="src-00434"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/73.txt`

Pesachim 73 - A destroyer on Shabbat
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1TToiES70-mmf3PwgcjQ2uzhTsq32zPq94uQncwMumwiW7tWLTcldNN1UgbvErPQpmcX2NonqUGOTVUkHTZ7sBtN9sb4Z7kEwER2ANEyyl4HkZiZQu8MfpdANWzoHwFkBiTTC4qK9gedA/s523/shabbat.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="383" data-original-width="523" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1TToiES70-mmf3PwgcjQ2uzhTsq32zPq94uQncwMumwiW7tWLTcldNN1UgbvErPQpmcX2NonqUGOTVUkHTZ7sBtN9sb4Z7kEwER2ANEyyl4HkZiZQu8MfpdANWzoHwFkBiTTC4qK9gedA/s320/shabbat.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>If people cannot eat the Passover offering's meat, and one slaughters the sheep for them, his act makes the sacrifice invalid. We had this rule <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/01/pesachim-61-who-comes-to-seder.html" target="_blank">earlier</a>. If he, moreover, does this on Shabbat, he is liable for a sin-offering. However, what did he do? There is a view that one who acts destructively on Shabbat does not violate Shabbat. Only constructive acts count. If so, why is he bringing a sin-offering?<div><br /></div><div>Rav Huna bar Chinana asked his son to ask Rav Zerika this question when he sees him. The answer was: here is what he accomplished, true, the sacrifice is invalid, but at least, if they mistakenly put its parts on the Altar,&nbsp; the parts can stay there.<br /><div><br /></div><div>The next question: if he slaughtered a sin-offering on Shabbat, outside the Temple, and as an idolatrous offering, he did many wrong things. But why is it counted in particular as a Shabbat violation? What positive effect did he accomplish? - At least, those who will be eating it are not eating a piece cut from a live animal - which is prohibited alike for Jews and non-Jews.</div></div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Shabbat by Mark Chagall</div>

---

### content/pesachim/74.txt

Pesachim 74 - How does one prepare the Passover lamb?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUM5pSyfADsl7NkdaH-kC7yhRmiCSJdpd2SkOkcWQfvJW0sR2pzMuR4yXQGj_2OIa90pQebWoi7wIOi5H89t3rWgNC5Ghyte_NOvdZ57Ub8LVeJqB7nXlVX8dAIRy3NpaK4dQsBYYpPwwa/s1024/Cornelius_van_Leemputten_Weidende_Schafe_und_H%25C3%25BCterin_1892.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="712" data-original-width="1024" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjUM5pSyfADsl7NkdaH-kC7yhRmiCSJdpd2SkOkcWQfvJW0sR2pzMuR4yXQGj_2OIa90pQebWoi7wIOi5H89t3rWgNC5Ghyte_NOvdZ57Ub8LVeJqB7nXlVX8dAIRy3NpaK4dQsBYYpPwwa/s320/Cornelius_van_Leemputten_Weidende_Schafe_und_H%25C3%25BCterin_1892.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The slaughtered lamb must be roasted on a spit. Here is the Torah's recipe: "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1826" target="_blank">Do not eat it raw or cooked in water, but only roasted over fire, including its head, its legs, and its internal organs.</a>" Now the details.<div><br /></div><div>They would bring a spit of pomegranate wood and push it into the animal's mouth until the spit passes through the anus. They would then put its legs and entrails inside it to fulfill "including its legs" instruction - that is what Rabbi Yosi says. But Rabbi Akiba counters that the legs are as if cooking inside the body. Rather, the legs and the entrails should hang outside the carcass to roast directly on the fire.</div><div><br /></div><div>Now questions. Why not use a metal spit? - Because it has to be roasted "over fire" and not over the hot spit warmed by the fire. Why pomegranate wood? - Because pomegranate is smooth and does not secrete any liquids, which would make it like roasting. How was the lamb's form called, with the legs and the entrails above its head? - the "helmeted kid" because it was in the manner of a warrior.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Shepherdess with her flock grazing&nbsp; by&nbsp;Cornelis Van Leemputten</div>

---

### content/pesachim/75.txt
<a id="src-00436"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/75.txt`

Pesachim 75 - Instructions on cooking and eating the Passover lamb
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEin8z1xaMt_gVe-Qa30-HVe9uTE2R5MjhB5keoy7x8SWU0o3K7hYV6CU6xjDOlp037hqVctj3DHlVX9a7BiHMRm3jAUb0w-rLef_YImBmL9Mt0VSYDtIp-sLaBL_WAPGS793JoHdXuc-E5A/s1280/Van+Gogh.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="899" data-original-width="1280" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEin8z1xaMt_gVe-Qa30-HVe9uTE2R5MjhB5keoy7x8SWU0o3K7hYV6CU6xjDOlp037hqVctj3DHlVX9a7BiHMRm3jAUb0w-rLef_YImBmL9Mt0VSYDtIp-sLaBL_WAPGS793JoHdXuc-E5A/s320/Van+Gogh.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Since the Passover offering must be "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1826" target="_blank">roasted over fire</a>," one must be careful when cooking. If they notice that the meat has touched the earthenware part of the oven while cooking, they need to scrape this part off. In this place, it was roasted due to the oven wall's heat, not open fire.<div><br /></div><div>If some gravy dripped onto the earthenware and then splatted back onto the meat, they should remove the meat in that place, to the depth of one finger - again, since in that place, it was boiled.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>After cooking, they can smear the dry meat with liquids. If they smeared it with oil, and that oil was "terumah" (the special gift that is given to the Kohanim priest that only they are allowed to eat) - here is what they do. If the people at the Seder are all Kohanim, they can eat the meat. But if some are regular Jews, they need to clean it. If the meat in this place was raw and did not absorb the oil, they simply rinse it. However, if it was fried and absorbent, they will need to remove the meat in that place, to the depth of one finger.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Still Life with Earthenware by Vincent van Gogh</div>

---
