Pesachim 76 - Passover lamb must be eaten
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhiW3qK0hx1kqKJqO04VYW1NmU9MjyZ-QjZvl744GGt0tgAtcGiRg3A_t7FHNI14lNMKGFOSR_SvxtLR9PvRrmewfa8OZ_i_H00__Pd9YssvuPouSUHP8ChdiTBpK05fjfpwme9DKiOMU_a/s1200/Jerusalem.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="771" data-original-width="1200" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhiW3qK0hx1kqKJqO04VYW1NmU9MjyZ-QjZvl744GGt0tgAtcGiRg3A_t7FHNI14lNMKGFOSR_SvxtLR9PvRrmewfa8OZ_i_H00__Pd9YssvuPouSUHP8ChdiTBpK05fjfpwme9DKiOMU_a/s320/Jerusalem.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>We <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/01/pesachim-66-how-rabbi-akiva-has-set-up.html" target="_blank">saw earlier</a> that if the community of those who came to Jerusalem celebrate Passover is ritually impure, they can all offer the sacrifice nevertheless. The instruction to bring it <b>in its appointed time</b> includes even the time when the community is impure. Since the whole purpose of bringing the offering is to eat it, the <b>appointed time</b> applies to eating as well.<div><br /></div><div>This is not always the case. There are five cases when the offering is brought but not eaten - when the community is impure. These other offerings may be flour or animal meat, and they would have to be burned.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;Jerusalem from the Mount of Olives by&nbsp;Frederic Edwin Church</div><div><br /></div><div><br /></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/77.txt
<a id="src-00438"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/77.txt`

Pesachim 77 - Can we completely dispense with ritual impurity?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyB55bpSyHl2nlwCq6y6n1c5PfXiPFIyQjuWWYV5m9ktTNQRFEQhfgzdf5fIDF7_oz9YfLxuOUDTxAUEyq00unlybRbFtA8LHkfCqs9zbawf4ETN_gUeOvrxl3qyVg_O5EneJ_7RO6Yv1P/s1280/1280px-Edouard_Manet_073_%2528Toter_Torero%2529.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="626" data-original-width="1280" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjyB55bpSyHl2nlwCq6y6n1c5PfXiPFIyQjuWWYV5m9ktTNQRFEQhfgzdf5fIDF7_oz9YfLxuOUDTxAUEyq00unlybRbFtA8LHkfCqs9zbawf4ETN_gUeOvrxl3qyVg_O5EneJ_7RO6Yv1P/s320/1280px-Edouard_Manet_073_%2528Toter_Torero%2529.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>In<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-76.html" target="_blank">&nbsp;the preceding pages</a>, we have discussed that the Passover offering is brought even when the community is ritually impure. How does this work? Do we say that the impurity is just pushed off, but we should try to observe its laws whenever we can? Or do we say that the impurity is to be completely ignored?<div><br /></div><div>The question is more general: can the community, being impure with corpse impurity, bring communal sacrifices? This depends on the power of the <i>tzitz</i>, a golden plate worn by the High Priest. Since the High Priest wears the <i>tzitz</i>, the sacrifices are valid - this is Rabbi Yehudah's opinion. Rabbi Shimon disagrees: even if the High Priest does not wear the <i>tzitz</i>, it still creates acceptance.</div><div><br /></div><div>Now Rabbi Shimon proves his point: on Yom Kippur, the High Priest changed into all-white garments and takes off the golden <i>tzitz<b> -</b></i>&nbsp;and nevertheless, the offerings are accepted! Rabbi Yehudah answers: forget about Yom Kippur! The impurity is anyway ignored when all are impure. We see that Rabbi Yehudah thinks that impurity is completely ignored, and Rabbi Shimon - that it is just pushed off.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: The Dead Man by Edouard Manet</div>

---

### content/pesachim/78.txt
<a id="src-00439"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/78.txt`

Pesachim 78 - The parts that go on the Altar
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh4HuPcauLSuv6zK8t5EMLlafR8v6mIG61fAaXQ9aV2jeeW8ocutF5XtyUVhP_2638Eo6ISYlqj22cp_tqQ733FNZEx2o8Q9n_dWgjOGEkifGs2A60rEvjfd0N5Smqp0NGSOGdSSu43E3RX/s600/Gabriel_Metsu_-_A_Young_Lady_at_Breakfast.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="504" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh4HuPcauLSuv6zK8t5EMLlafR8v6mIG61fAaXQ9aV2jeeW8ocutF5XtyUVhP_2638Eo6ISYlqj22cp_tqQ733FNZEx2o8Q9n_dWgjOGEkifGs2A60rEvjfd0N5Smqp0NGSOGdSSu43E3RX/s320/Gabriel_Metsu_-_A_Young_Lady_at_Breakfast.jpg" /></a></div>When the Passover offering is brought, certain parts of the animal (some fats, kidney, diaphragm, and liver) go on the Altar and are burnt there. However, if the meat becomes ritually impure, there is no point in further service, putting the fats on the Altar or throwing the blood. The only purpose of the Passover sacrifice is to eat the meat, and since the impure meat cannot be eaten, we stop there.<p></p><p>However, if something happened to the fats that go on the Altar, but the meat is still OK - we continue, throw the blood, and eat the meat. Incidentally, in our discussion, we have returned to the normal case of the community being pure. Had the community been impure, we would eat the meat even if it was impure and ask no questions about the remaining parts' purity.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;A Young Lady at Breakfast by Gabriël Metsu</p>

---

### content/pesachim/79.txt
<a id="src-00440"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/79.txt`

Pesachim 79 - How many pure and how many not pure?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZLclzeCL9WHXByZjHw8dCryul7CZGzuIZqEtNIvC4HrV1eGtQII1RxMy3QkQKuLP5ejPUdjf-4YMPhKK1pa-CgY_BSRfGyk4r86GpRvxDeWbJ3FWZhMVoe7UbqStsg0QEduSR-vuqaKyS/s564/better+color.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; display: inline !important; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="424" data-original-width="564" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZLclzeCL9WHXByZjHw8dCryul7CZGzuIZqEtNIvC4HrV1eGtQII1RxMy3QkQKuLP5ejPUdjf-4YMPhKK1pa-CgY_BSRfGyk4r86GpRvxDeWbJ3FWZhMVoe7UbqStsg0QEduSR-vuqaKyS/s320/better+color.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>We often mentioned a situation where the community is not pure and is therefore allowed to bring the Passover sacrifice even in ritual impurity. But what do we mean by "community?" The whole world, Israel, Jerusalem? For this purpose, we only count those who have assembled for Passover to bring the offerings. Even here, we only need the majority. So, if more than half of those assembled to bring the offering are not ritually pure, everyone now brings it in impurity.<p></p><p>Also, if the Kohanim priests were impure, even though the community is pure, they all join and celebrate in impurity.</p><p>However, if only a minority of the community are impure, then the majority still celebrates, but the remaining minority gets a second chance thirty days later, on the so-called "Second Passover" or <i><a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/01/pesachim-67.html" target="_blank">Pesach Sheni</a>.&nbsp;</i></p><p>Art: Jerusalem seen from Mount Josaphat by Auguste de Forbin</p>

---

### content/pesachim/8.txt
<a id="src-00441"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/8.txt`

Pesachim 8 – The light of a candle
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtOviZrFDKZZVPiPy0lw2A2_vY3WcBhRTXxJ-Uyiy4GLW4ZqIlkLI7TXTzxJvGtRrWqF2_t-WdMDrFtsdHRhi0f8GkTA7BKO-IM_brWDnmHCtEuAX26MDQUBYBLnBrEuw6fB0-mJ5c1zYz/s600/Boy+with+a+Torch+by+Matthias+Stomer.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgtOviZrFDKZZVPiPy0lw2A2_vY3WcBhRTXxJ-Uyiy4GLW4ZqIlkLI7TXTzxJvGtRrWqF2_t-WdMDrFtsdHRhi0f8GkTA7BKO-IM_brWDnmHCtEuAX26MDQUBYBLnBrEuw6fB0-mJ5c1zYz/s320/Boy+with+a+Torch+by+Matthias+Stomer.jpg" width="267" /></a></div>
We mentioned before that one should search for chametz using the light of a candle. Why a candle? It comes through a chain of associations. Chametz should “not be found.” This leads to remembering Joseph who “searched and found” (a divining goblet in the sack of Benjamin). The “found” leads to the words of the prophet who promises that God will look for the errors of the people of the city of Jerusalem using the light of candles, and not “find” any. And finally “candles” leads to the words of King Solomon that “The soul of a man is the candle of God, which God uses to inspect the deeds of man."
<br />
<br />
Why do we need the last connection, from “candles” to “candle?” It is already pretty clear and close by then! – Because one might think that searching with candles is leniency, and God will overlook some errors precisely because of using candles. To show that this is untrue,  we bring the last proof of the candle being the light of God.
<br />
<br />
Still, why not use a torch? First, because with the torch he will be afraid to examine nooks and crevices, since he may cause a fire. Also, a torch gives unsteady flame, while that of a candle is constant. Yet another reason is that one carries a torch behind himself, and the candle he carries in front.
<br />
<br />
Art: Boy with a Torch by Matthias Stomer (1600 -  1650)

---

### content/pesachim/80.txt
<a id="src-00442"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/80.txt`

Pesachim 80 - The forgiving power of the tzitz
<a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/11/yoma-7-tzitz.html" target="_blank"><i></i></a><i><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/11/yoma-7-tzitz.html" target="_blank"></a><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgTNWiIUec80QX8k015PVKNHITsQ_MPjFZpy1dfyxpS8aGhv0fYqbWool8-JkNgT93js2YuRS2k2avoKeV1g5BjQTbgP5P_il0eaAAHrcLRUT_z9Fi3jyH-1AQnuI_AMkOA77UoJSWTShkx/s1024/Charles_Emile_Champmartin_-_Th%25C3%25A9odore_G%25C3%25A9ricault_on_His_Deathbed_-_1937.502_-_Art_Institute_of_Chicago.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="832" data-original-width="1024" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgTNWiIUec80QX8k015PVKNHITsQ_MPjFZpy1dfyxpS8aGhv0fYqbWool8-JkNgT93js2YuRS2k2avoKeV1g5BjQTbgP5P_il0eaAAHrcLRUT_z9Fi3jyH-1AQnuI_AMkOA77UoJSWTShkx/s320/Charles_Emile_Champmartin_-_Th%25C3%25A9odore_G%25C3%25A9ricault_on_His_Deathbed_-_1937.502_-_Art_Institute_of_Chicago.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Tzitz</i> is the golden head plate worn by the High Priest. It fixed the defects of sacrifices, but not all the defects. Thus, if someone brought his Passover offering and even threw its blood on the Altar, but then they discovered that the meat or the blood became ritually impure, it is the <i>tzitz</i> that effects the acceptance. What is the use of acceptance if the meat cannot eaten? At least, he has fulfilled his obligation and won't have to bring another sacrifice. He will eat matzah and other things at the Seder.<div><br /></div><div>What if they discovered that he himself was ritually impure? Here the <i>tzitz</i> does not help, and he will have to bring the Passover offering a month later, on <i>Pesach Sheni</i>. However, here is a special exception. If he was impure due to the "impurity of the depth," his Passover offering is valid, and he will not have to bring another one - all due to the <i>tzitz</i>. What is this special "impurity of the depth?" - This is something that absolutely nobody knew about, such as a corpse under the house, unknown to anybody, that was discovered later.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Study of the Head of a Corpse by Charles Emile Champmartin</div><div><br /></div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/81.txt
<a id="src-00443"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/81.txt`

Pesachim 81 - What happens to the ritually impure meat?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjoUjq_wcadBznWpKPr45JQ7IrGdPUlL1lvluyGyXV0ztRVr6TSaGXnTHXPqdTMfWTL3TLxj_S48URsc2QJPmZHLUe_rBF7yKc3mwChWi8Vu1RlPS1PBljHNmKYHkYmInMcdfWoJxkLZSK1/s800/Dutch+farm+worker.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="800" data-original-width="714" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjoUjq_wcadBznWpKPr45JQ7IrGdPUlL1lvluyGyXV0ztRVr6TSaGXnTHXPqdTMfWTL3TLxj_S48URsc2QJPmZHLUe_rBF7yKc3mwChWi8Vu1RlPS1PBljHNmKYHkYmInMcdfWoJxkLZSK1/s320/Dutch+farm+worker.jpg" /></a></div>There was a place on the Temple Mount specifically designated for burning invalid offering. So, if a Passover offering became ritually impure, the whole thing or the majority of its meat - it was burnt in this place. When burning the offering, one was allowed to use the Temple wood. Even though he was using Temple property for his purposes, this was allowed - to prevent people from eating disqualified meat when they faced the expense of buying the wood to burn it.<p></p><p>If only a small portion of the sacrificial meat became impure, one would take it home and burn it there, in the courtyard or on the roof, and use his own wood. That would have to happen within the City of Jerusalem, called today, "The Old City." Cheapskates would burn even small amounts of impure meat next to the Temple - to take advantage of the Temple wood.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Dutch farmworker gathering wood by Hans Heysen</p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/82.txt
<a id="src-00444"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/82.txt`

Pesachim 82 - Took the Passover meat out of Jerusalem!
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0NyxEnbP6Iw73ELvUYCsV0hlfh89gZBnZZvnI-sW0ml_n008iw0Vwe37PqMmZ5C211L-u9c5a4FWk3d7OoSYyoIEp3tBRh2U_PRNTpOaruUOTOgBe7Zfo_zAaimavPCrKBI77LawIbbM3/s570/dying-man.jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="570" data-original-width="441" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg0NyxEnbP6Iw73ELvUYCsV0hlfh89gZBnZZvnI-sW0ml_n008iw0Vwe37PqMmZ5C211L-u9c5a4FWk3d7OoSYyoIEp3tBRh2U_PRNTpOaruUOTOgBe7Zfo_zAaimavPCrKBI77LawIbbM3/s320/dying-man.jpeg" /></a></div>The meat of the Passover lamb must stay within the walls of Jerusalem (the Old City). If one takes it out, it is disqualified. If this happens before the Passover Holiday itself, one must burn the disqualified meat right away. He cannot eat it, and any mitzvah should be done immediately - in this case, it is the mitzvah of burning disqualified offerings.<p></p><p>By contrast, if the owners of the sacrifice became ritually impure or died, we know that nobody will be able to eat the meat, but we cannot burn it. So, the meat is left overnight, and then it becomes the leftover sacrifice, and it can and must be burned. One cannot burn on on the first day of Passover because it is a Holiday, so he burns it on the following day.</p><p>Rabbi Yochanan ben Berokah compares the last case with the death of the sons of Aharon, where the sacrifice was burned immediately, and says that we should do the same.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Dying Man by Isidoro Grunhut</p>

---

### content/pesachim/83.txt
<a id="src-00445"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/83.txt`

Pesachim 83 - The leftovers from the Seder
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizBly2P0YJhor47DBbIxmis3lCCHTt_e9-b8wl66XyPQ2u1sO-xlM8zxUx4SSYDnhOwRIHkLzW2Adt31rD_ozhNmHv0cL0k5eb3Ra0A10zZ8iC941TViSXoga2mfhgzmBdDPN5mrTJL3XS/s564/leftovers.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="399" data-original-width="564" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEizBly2P0YJhor47DBbIxmis3lCCHTt_e9-b8wl66XyPQ2u1sO-xlM8zxUx4SSYDnhOwRIHkLzW2Adt31rD_ozhNmHv0cL0k5eb3Ra0A10zZ8iC941TViSXoga2mfhgzmBdDPN5mrTJL3XS/s320/leftovers.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The leftover parts of the sacrificial meat that was served at the Seder also require special care. Take, for example, the bones. "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1863" target="_blank">Do not break any of its bones</a>," said the Torah. Therefore, the marrow inside the bones cannot be removed." But any edible part of a sacrifice becomes <i>notar</i>, or leftover, on the next day and has to be burned. So leftover bones must be burned.<p></p><p>The same is true for the sinews and leftover meat of the sacrifice. They all must be burned on the next day after the Seder. If that day fell out on Shabbat, they wait till yet the next day. Although it is a mitzvah, the burning of the leftover does not override either Shabbat or the Holiday.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Still Life with a Goat Head&nbsp; Jusepe de Ribera</p>

---

### content/pesachim/84.txt
<a id="src-00446"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/84.txt`

Pesachim 84 - Take the meat but leave the bones
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgvgN76ge1CbGLthQkKb11BvhzxEcNzIuXoeWZaEiaigUvE-_UsYko54zs4jQIimW7OVFem24D91roaqE4lAwgydsLWP64BFnwWCBr3ah6SgfjrdbIYkF9W_ek0kIyflg8bHrRoX2-4vRlu/s1200/meat.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="999" data-original-width="1200" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgvgN76ge1CbGLthQkKb11BvhzxEcNzIuXoeWZaEiaigUvE-_UsYko54zs4jQIimW7OVFem24D91roaqE4lAwgydsLWP64BFnwWCBr3ah6SgfjrdbIYkF9W_ek0kIyflg8bHrRoX2-4vRlu/s320/meat.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>At the Seder, there should be enough meat of the Passover sacrifice for everybody. "Enough" means the volume of an average olive. But what is considered "meat?" - Any part that will be tender enough to eat in a grown-up animal is considered "meat." But any part that will harden in a grown-up ox is not considered meat towards the olive volume.<p></p><p>We already mentioned that one is <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-83.html">not supposed to break the bones</a> of a Passover sacrifice. One can even be punished for doing so (of course, the usual rules of giving him a warning not to do it, within a few seconds before the act, apply). However, one is not punished for another prohibited action - leaving the meat over till morning. Why not? Some say - because you cannot punish for not doing. Others - that anytime something is prohibited but a correction is suggested - here, by burning it, you can't punish for it.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Butcher's shop by&nbsp;Annibale Carracci</p><p><br /></p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/85.txt
<a id="src-00447"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/85.txt`

Pesachim 85 - The doors and the windows of Jerusalem
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWXxsyZrYeDTgu5Zcpc2Isd0b9O2yI0TaxQmGm2VrLEY2PlYywhwKqaw69RZLcxBB6wsGp7uFmiFnySaUuh8o1ML7OZx_N7Zna8xRNqAULcZPFf5v_EwGOXpxSDA1hh1rODzsdR3-q4jCr/s1080/bluedoor.jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="1080" data-original-width="880" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWXxsyZrYeDTgu5Zcpc2Isd0b9O2yI0TaxQmGm2VrLEY2PlYywhwKqaw69RZLcxBB6wsGp7uFmiFnySaUuh8o1ML7OZx_N7Zna8xRNqAULcZPFf5v_EwGOXpxSDA1hh1rODzsdR3-q4jCr/s320/bluedoor.jpeg" /></a></div>The Passover sacrifice has to remain within the walls of Jerusalem (Old City). If it is taken out, it becomes disqualified, cannot be eaten, and has to be burned.<p></p><p>What happens if a part of the sacrifice protrudes outside this boundary? His problem is that he cannot chop the protruding portion off because he <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-83.html" target="_blank">cannot&nbsp;break the sacrifice bones</a>. Therefore, he cuts into the flesh until he reaches the bone, then peels the flesh away until he gets to the join, and now he can cut off the entire bone. He does not have to take such precautions for other sacrifices but just chops it with a cleaver.</p><p>What about the doors (which, in an ancient city, could have significant depth)? The doorway, which is also called "doorjamb," is considered as outside of Jerusalem. By contrast, the windows are considered inside. Why such a difference? They should all be considered as inside Jerusalem. However, when the city was originally consecrated, the gateways were not included on purpose. A&nbsp;<i>metzorah</i> (ritual leper) could take refuge there, in the summer - from the sun, and in the winter - from the rain.</p><p>Art:&nbsp; Blue Door by Andrew Wyeth</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/86.txt
<a id="src-00448"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/86.txt`

Pesachim 86 - Two groups of people, two Seders
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhraZPAN9RPNU_-9tBpTtCvVGzfbL6NALXZqXrQ8PkMEFcSN2rn_9AyoWA_hbWXKe1jAG1v5Y7RQNhWQlOc4KzXF3N2LZ8W-8hf-25xgkkY2DNhEswGu5_yQtqu8dmtCE8D-0RajNNFyPdV/s599/511px-Jan_van_Bijlert_-_Young_Man_Drinking_a_Glass_of_Wine_-_WGA02184.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="599" data-original-width="511" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhraZPAN9RPNU_-9tBpTtCvVGzfbL6NALXZqXrQ8PkMEFcSN2rn_9AyoWA_hbWXKe1jAG1v5Y7RQNhWQlOc4KzXF3N2LZ8W-8hf-25xgkkY2DNhEswGu5_yQtqu8dmtCE8D-0RajNNFyPdV/s320/511px-Jan_van_Bijlert_-_Young_Man_Drinking_a_Glass_of_Wine_-_WGA02184.jpg" /></a></div>To eat a Passover lamb, people had to register for it first. Once they are registered and the time to eat it comes, they cannot change their minds. They must eat it in the house where they started and cannot change this either. However, before starting the Seder, if they decide to separate into two groups, they are perfectly allowed to do so.<p></p><p>There was a custom to dilute the intense wine served at the table with hot water. The water would come from a kettle, and the kettle could be positioned between the groups - again, this separation created no problem. However, the waiter who would be pouring this water had to be careful to eat with only one group. When he is serving the other group members, he keeps his mouth shut until he returns to his own group. A bride who is at the Seder with her new family for the first time can turn the face away, not observing the rules of the waiter.</p><p>Rav Huna once came to a new place. His actions seemed unusual to the people there, and they questioned him about every one of them. For example, he said that his name was Rav Huna. That seemed presumptuous - just give you name, no "Rav!" - He said, I was called Rav Huna since childhood. When he drank, he did not turn his face away. That looked immodest to them. He said: "We learned - only a bride needs to turn her face away!"</p><p>Art: Young Man Drinking a Glass of Wine by Jan van Bijlert</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/87.txt
<a id="src-00449"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/87.txt`

Pesachim 87 - A woman in her husband's house
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgVST-JiUVzruC9HCDQ_60KTRROKvgQ2D9PvFDX8xuEJDPJ7dWqGLTtUGVsG297Opof7f2sNJ9h_rzYsoIb1hGIDaAJfjkMuZcUjdU8iSAUPk1n1XvYjuo9w9KHLRVQcEPGhyphenhyphenFjlPcEkmdM/s599/441px-Jordaens_Portrait_of_a_Young_Married_Couple.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="599" data-original-width="441" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgVST-JiUVzruC9HCDQ_60KTRROKvgQ2D9PvFDX8xuEJDPJ7dWqGLTtUGVsG297Opof7f2sNJ9h_rzYsoIb1hGIDaAJfjkMuZcUjdU8iSAUPk1n1XvYjuo9w9KHLRVQcEPGhyphenhyphenFjlPcEkmdM/s320/441px-Jordaens_Portrait_of_a_Young_Married_Couple.jpg" /></a></div>Everyone who participates in a Seder should be registered for the Passover sacrifice beforehand. Sometimes, one may even be registered for two lambs. How?<p></p><p>Consider a woman who has recently married and lives with her husband in his house. She did not say whose sacrifice she wanted to eat, but we can assume she will eat her husband's lamb. So, if her father also slaughtered a sacrifice for her, she would eat her husband's one. However, if she goes back home for the first Seder (as was often the custom) and her husband and father slaughter a lamb, she eats whichever she chooses.&nbsp;</p><p>The last rule sounds strange. It tells us that the wife's later decision affects the earlier sacrifice. This is called retroactive designation, and it is usually not allowed. It's like saying that this is what she wanted all along - even if she did not know it. So the Talmud changes the circumstances and says, "You know when she chose it? - Before the slaughter!"</p><p>By association, the Talmud talks about God's love for the Israeli nation as for a beloved.</p><p>Art: A young married couple by Jacob Jordaens</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/88.txt
<a id="src-00450"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/88.txt`

Pesachim 88 - Half-slave
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1F8aouRAlY6UcxwxHSnLbgwMKwNRlyxSmwIXPKM5CVLNj4rA3vfCdkuALmvP81M4vAS8pQa9LY2YE9H-seXkGVZ9dg1WSwuiDF2ict2Zjqhl3-ozyGQp3bYUNVDgSzcqiL_TUJcLYr5J4/s2048/soutine.jpg" style="clear: left; display: inline !important; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="2048" data-original-width="1514" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1F8aouRAlY6UcxwxHSnLbgwMKwNRlyxSmwIXPKM5CVLNj4rA3vfCdkuALmvP81M4vAS8pQa9LY2YE9H-seXkGVZ9dg1WSwuiDF2ict2Zjqhl3-ozyGQp3bYUNVDgSzcqiL_TUJcLYr5J4/s320/soutine.jpg" /></a></div>A <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2016/01/gittin-41-slave-of-two-masters.html" target="_blank">slave of two masters</a> is a common theme in the Talmud. On Passover, if both owners registered him to eat of their sacrifice, he cannot eat of either. Similarly, a half-slave cannot eat the sacrifice because it is assumed that the master only wanted to register his part of the slave, not the free part. (A half-slave is a hint to a person who is governed both by his good inclination and his even inclination.) If so, why did we learn in another source that the slave can eat the sacrifice? - That is talking about the case when the slave's two owners are at peace with each other.<p></p><p>If one sent his slave to slaughter a sacrifice for him but did not tell which we wanted, a young goat or a lamb, he can eat whichever animal the slave chose. We can presume that he relies on the choice of his slave.</p><p>If the slave slaughtered both a young goat and a lamb, the master eats what was slaughtered first. However, this rule is only for a king and queen who absolutely do not care what to eat because they have everything. Other people do have at least some preference, and since we cannot ascertain what it is, we cannot allow them to eat of any.</p><p>Art: Carcass of Beef by Chaim Soutine</p><div><br /></div><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/89.txt
<a id="src-00451"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/89.txt`

Pesachim 89 - A guest who ate too much
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPd0wOz8j67jgHIGnJk4seveSSfD0d2V8GhcKTWrUrK4KzlQHf_9PnKv7mgII5ht1iFafLuwMynlFqdnCNobuBHcQkQYX1ET8fCd7NcAc044_W_3e2KaS3jhhQkpthPDAgpwL0ObfJeYUr/s850/Diego_Vel%25C3%25A1zquez_016.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="850" data-original-width="800" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjPd0wOz8j67jgHIGnJk4seveSSfD0d2V8GhcKTWrUrK4KzlQHf_9PnKv7mgII5ht1iFafLuwMynlFqdnCNobuBHcQkQYX1ET8fCd7NcAc044_W_3e2KaS3jhhQkpthPDAgpwL0ObfJeYUr/s320/Diego_Vel%25C3%25A1zquez_016.jpg" /></a></div>If one invites his friends to the Seder and registers them to eat of the Passover sacrifice - all without consulting the other members of the group - they can tell him, "Take your portion and eat it together with your friends." That is because they invited him originally to make sure that all meat is properly eaten - but not to bring other personalities into the picture, even if they give him his due portion.&nbsp;<p></p><p>Now a question: if one of the guests just eats too much and too fast, can the guests at the Seder tell him, "Take your due portion and leave?" Can they find the precedent in the earlier case of one inviting more guests, or can he argue back and say, "You accepted me!" The Talmud goes through a few possible precedents until it finds convincing proof that the glutton can be asked to leave.</p><p>A similar story happened to Rav Pappa and Rav Huna, who sat together (not on Passover) to eat bread. While Rav Huna ate one piece, Rav Pappa ate four. So Rav Huna wanted to separate, but Rav Pappa argued that "You accepted me!" They went through all the precedents mentioned above until Rav Huna quoted a decisive one and separated from Rav Pappa. He then joined with Ravina, but Ravina ate two times faster than even Rav Pappa. So Ran Huna exclaimed, "Give me a hundred Pappas and not one Ravina!"</p><p>Art: Peasants' Dinner by Diego Velazquez</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/9.txt
<a id="src-00452"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/9.txt`

Pesachim 9 – Weasel drags bread from house to house
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuIILQ14Irvn-lYb42dgnH-l7mjfSE7stX-zvkTAMQ8qIVkcpP23YjSiFzgo4LCrQKktsh30awVWcaQqMn_Lnki-GBFZ-RUHlaq5h5QAoXeFe_EDS1hzKzm7cVyok07tJMhn7oi9Cg0l5R/s600/A+Weasel+by+Edward+Lear.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="212" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjuIILQ14Irvn-lYb42dgnH-l7mjfSE7stX-zvkTAMQ8qIVkcpP23YjSiFzgo4LCrQKktsh30awVWcaQqMn_Lnki-GBFZ-RUHlaq5h5QAoXeFe_EDS1hzKzm7cVyok07tJMhn7oi9Cg0l5R/s320/A+Weasel+by+Edward+Lear.jpg" width="320" /></a>After one searches his home for chametz, he does not have to worry that perhaps a weasel will now bring bread from another house. The same is true of one's room: once it is searched, one need not think that a weasel might bring it there from another room. This is true because if one is to be concerned, he would have to suspect that a weasel brought it from another courtyard or another town, and there would be no end to his worries.
<br />
<br />
However, as the Talmud notes, this rule is good only if one does not see a weasel or a mouse, going into his house <b>with bread</b>. If he does, then he has to be concerned. But why? Why not say that the mouse ate that bread?! After all, we have multiple rulings which assume that if a mouse or a weasel are found in a place where possibly ritually impure meat was dropped, then it was surely eaten, and the place is therefore ritually clean!? – True, they will eat the meat, but as for the bread, they will leave some over and hide it.
<br />
<br />
And yet, we do worry about weasels, since all food that is left over after the search for chametz is hidden and not put in an easily accessible place – obviously because a weasel may take it away. Abaye explained, “Yes, the weasel may hide it just before Pesach when soon there will be no bread available, but not earlier when there is plenty.” Rava objected, “Is a weasel a prophetess that she knows that soon there will be no bread?! – Rather, the danger is that the weasel will take it away in one's presence, and then he will have to search again.”
<br />
<br />
Art: A Weasel by Edward Lear

---

### content/pesachim/90.txt
<a id="src-00453"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/90.txt`

Pesachim 90 - Just-in-time purity
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGtfxdZu7SL35IPWvDA-ji0TNV_KLwlyljlb8qnd80bC40z_nBnrIrPdsrJjrojsETdgdDXK7bZ_5IXI-nDB01cW1t1RrprUQX9yInYZUrRk9CdAl33k44rlldDhaRk2kro3EqWy1FDDWL/s1280/1280px-August_Cappelen_-_Waterfall_in_Telemark_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="955" data-original-width="1280" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgGtfxdZu7SL35IPWvDA-ji0TNV_KLwlyljlb8qnd80bC40z_nBnrIrPdsrJjrojsETdgdDXK7bZ_5IXI-nDB01cW1t1RrprUQX9yInYZUrRk9CdAl33k44rlldDhaRk2kro3EqWy1FDDWL/s320/1280px-August_Cappelen_-_Waterfall_in_Telemark_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The time to bring the Passover sacrifice is the afternoon just before the Holiday of Passover. If one is ritually impure in the afternoon but will be pure the next day, that is, when evening comes and the Holiday of Passover begins, they can slaughter a sacrifice for him. Even though he is not pure now, he will be pure when he sits down to eat it at the Seder.<p></p><p>What could be an example of this? A <i><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/06/definition-of-term-zav.html" target="_blank">zav</a></i> (a special kind of male impurity) who experienced two discharges must count seven days without discharges and immerse himself in a flowing spring. After that, he is pure once the night begins. So, that is exactly the case we are talking about if today he counted his seventh day. Even if this zav had three discharges, which obligates him in an additional offering - they can still slaughter the Passover lamb for him. He will be pure at night, and he will bring the additional offering later on, but he can come to the Seder and eat.</p><p>Art: Waterfall in Telemark by August Cappelen</p>

---

### content/pesachim/91.txt
<a id="src-00454"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/91.txt`

Pesachim 91 - Integrity
<p><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-90.html" target="_blank"></a></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGCeAKu1Zce8Svq8CHxJnLu2WeZ92D6zkkmV84Cc4D7MHx72-10YiFcjcnSZTGsQ_A6O3_FlfNjp9xpJRH0bigNfyahXfwQu8RJMB3SFVlKqCE1eZaAWlv_oiIv7C5pIyDjgYqy5WQIGIH/s600/the-prisoner-1882.jpg%2521Large.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="401" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGCeAKu1Zce8Svq8CHxJnLu2WeZ92D6zkkmV84Cc4D7MHx72-10YiFcjcnSZTGsQ_A6O3_FlfNjp9xpJRH0bigNfyahXfwQu8RJMB3SFVlKqCE1eZaAWlv_oiIv7C5pIyDjgYqy5WQIGIH/s320/the-prisoner-1882.jpg%2521Large.jpg" /></a></div>Earlier, we saw cases where people were not ritually pure in the afternoon when the Passover sacrifice was brought but would become pure at night when its meat was eaten at the Seder. So it was allowed to bring a sacrifice on their behalf.<p></p><p>Now, we will see cases where the people may become impure by nighttime. The priests will still slaughter the lamb for them anyway. But, since there was a chance of them becoming impure, they would need to be combined with others who were definitely pure - or else the meat might have no eaters at all.</p><p>For example, take the case of a rescue worker who is clearing a house's debris where someone may have been trapped. He may find and save a person or find a corpse, touch it, and become impure. Or it could be someone who was promised a release from prison - because the jailers may change their minds.</p><p>In the last case, Rabbi Yochanan commented that if it is a Jewish prison, he can rely on their promise because the Jewish courts have integrity: "<a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/e/et/et2103.htm" target="_blank">The remainder of Israel will not perform iniquity and will not speak lies</a>."</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Prisoner by Vladimir Makovsky</p>

---

### content/pesachim/92.txt
<a id="src-00455"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/92.txt`

Pesachim 92 - Pesach Sheni
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgpluhE9Kp5qokGG7pLDqv5UB1y6H_riq5SAugpEgwN68Ilrc12uKMaaCeL2AlLc_4-4AU0mtCEJ2H9P91EpyuE8J3DWsWnmAR2AV9fVu7cj9kge6Mg9BFMiXxoKlTJawiKRWzLjzyZTKqx/s600/Edvard_Munch_-_Galloping_Horse_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="488" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgpluhE9Kp5qokGG7pLDqv5UB1y6H_riq5SAugpEgwN68Ilrc12uKMaaCeL2AlLc_4-4AU0mtCEJ2H9P91EpyuE8J3DWsWnmAR2AV9fVu7cj9kge6Mg9BFMiXxoKlTJawiKRWzLjzyZTKqx/s320/Edvard_Munch_-_Galloping_Horse_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" /></a></div>If someone was prevented from participating in the Passover celebration and could not bring and eat the sacrifice - he gets a second chance thirty days later. This second chance is called <i>Pesach Sheni</i>, or Second Passover. What could be the circumstances?<p></p><p>"<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=9#P3973" target="_blank">If someone contracted corpse impurity or he was far away from the Temple</a>" are the two reasons given by the Torah. While corpse impurity is well-defined: one touches a corpse or happens to be under the same roof with a corpse, other impurity types lead to discussions; for example, we discussed <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-90.html" target="_blank">one who will become pure by the Seder time</a>. But what does it mean to be far away? The simple understanding is that it is the distance one can travel on foot on Passover's eve, starting out in the morning and arriving at the Temple in the afternoon.&nbsp;</p><p>But what if he has a fast horse or a car? Rabbi Nachman says that if he asked someone to bring a sacrifice for him, it is definitely valid. Not only that, he deserves a special blessing for his desire to do a mitzvah. Rav Sheshet, however, says that being too far away is similar to being ritually impure: both are barred from the Passover sacrifice this time, and both will have to make up for it thirty days later.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Galloping Horse by Edvard Munch</p>

---

### content/pesachim/93.txt
<a id="src-00456"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/93.txt`

Pesachim 93 - How far is far?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiiVbki7Zi1xOFRI2z9_xaEHdN8iLzOslwPsc-iaKXW-0IKoSTJSVi3t43t8UCRDaJcns45QBpCeeycOJJ6y4Ke9AdvNCRP9sFYecvP88986Dys018gr3AR3wXNJUYq5Qc_R5R_qE5iMUFa/s1242/MB-Cai-03_Caillebotte_Paar-beim-Spaziergang_1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="993" data-original-width="1242" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiiVbki7Zi1xOFRI2z9_xaEHdN8iLzOslwPsc-iaKXW-0IKoSTJSVi3t43t8UCRDaJcns45QBpCeeycOJJ6y4Ke9AdvNCRP9sFYecvP88986Dys018gr3AR3wXNJUYq5Qc_R5R_qE5iMUFa/s320/MB-Cai-03_Caillebotte_Paar-beim-Spaziergang_1.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>We <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-92.html" target="_blank">learned</a> that if one happens to be far away from the Temple on Passover and cannot bring and eat a Passover offering, he can do it thirty days later, on Pesach Sheni. We also said that "too far" is the distance one can travel on foot on Passover's eve, starting out in the morning and arriving at the Temple in the afternoon.<div><br /></div><div>In practical terms, this is the distance <a href="https://www.google.com/maps/dir/Temple+Mount,+Jerusalem/Modi'in-Maccabim-Re'ut,+Israel/@31.8364518,35.0415955,12z/data=!3m1!4b1!4m14!4m13!1m5!1m1!1s0x150329c91f33ffdb:0x6d2bbd5ce62d60ab!2m2!1d35.2359927!2d31.7781161!1m5!1m1!1s0x1502cdc4ba7c9a35:0xaf5f6cbfe5133203!2m2!1d35.010397!2d31.890267!3e0" target="_blank">from Modiin to the Temple</a>. Then you draw a circle with the Temple Mount as a center and with this radius. In real life, one would have to consider different opinions of understanding this rule, not just measure.&nbsp;</div><div><br /></div><div>Rabbi Eliezer disagrees: as long as one is outside the Temple Courtyard, that is already too far, and one is exempt from punishment for not bringing a Passover offering. Rabbi Yosi offers support for it: in the Torah scroll, there are dots above the word "distant." Such dots usually indicate a doubt. In this case, he is just somewhat distant from the Temple, that is, outside the Courtyard.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Couple on a Walk by Gustave Caillebotte</div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/94.txt
<a id="src-00457"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/94.txt`

Pesachim 94 - Distances
<p><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-93.html" target="_blank"></a></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgY5vFhzlfWLDTF-RRHjV1NqpwijFTg_QcGNjcNocCT4GaMcZYz9si1JDrWVr3Qh99SZECfTEaXzds_DXwr8iAVgrYLK94bLDWNeFiL9bYSsNzwya9FwTec9C1gePKDVJmu9HxGGSntFQ1q/s900/2-a-scholar-in-his-study-salomon-koninck.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="900" data-original-width="749" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgY5vFhzlfWLDTF-RRHjV1NqpwijFTg_QcGNjcNocCT4GaMcZYz9si1JDrWVr3Qh99SZECfTEaXzds_DXwr8iAVgrYLK94bLDWNeFiL9bYSsNzwya9FwTec9C1gePKDVJmu9HxGGSntFQ1q/s320/2-a-scholar-in-his-study-salomon-koninck.jpg" /></a></div>Earlier, we said that being far from the Temple means being at the distance of Modiin, five&nbsp;<i>mil</i>,&nbsp; or 10,000 <i>amah</i>&nbsp;(steps). A person walks forty <i>mil</i>&nbsp;a day. From here, we can calculate many other distances.<p></p><p>For example, Egypt is four hundred <i>parsah</i> by four hundred <i>parsah</i> (where <i>parsah</i> is eight thousand square amah), Kush is sixty times larger, the world is sixty times larger than Kush, and Eden is sixty times larger than the world.</p><p>What do all these numbers mean, and why do they matter? They are hints to spiritual journeys. For example, when earlier we learned about a one who was impure on the first Pesach, it is a hint that he made his soul impure on his first reincarnation.&nbsp;Now he needs to come back again (this is his second Pesach). For a righteous person, mistakes in learning are considered intentional errors. However, he is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-93.html" target="_blank">free from punishment</a> if he fails to bring his Passover offering. The more one learns the more one understands these hints.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;A Scholar in His Study by Salomon Koninck</p>

---

### content/pesachim/95.txt
<a id="src-00458"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/95.txt`

Pesachim 95 - Compare first and second Passover
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhPaGLnJjuKRp_d3eCNOIL5w3lGi4MnW6BOSfzSqtSGmAAc9AWqUEpvHyR_tKuVMd8zvQicReYHwHi1WxFZYzgwl0jDFpPSZQrc0pOQvfYyvpV7i_4qt-3FHJOpf1t_7Bswp9gQ5Qdr2NSM/s833/1981.1_Basket+of+Bread_web.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="825" data-original-width="833" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhPaGLnJjuKRp_d3eCNOIL5w3lGi4MnW6BOSfzSqtSGmAAc9AWqUEpvHyR_tKuVMd8zvQicReYHwHi1WxFZYzgwl0jDFpPSZQrc0pOQvfYyvpV7i_4qt-3FHJOpf1t_7Bswp9gQ5Qdr2NSM/s320/1981.1_Basket+of+Bread_web.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The second Passover is one's second chance. It happens a month after the Passover, and its laws are somewhat relaxed. <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/07/pesachim-22-not-eating-and-not-using.html" target="_blank">On the first Passover, he cannot eat chametz, cannot own it, and cannot benefit from it</a>. On the second one, one can happily own both chametz and matzah at the same time.<p></p><p>There is also a difference in prayer: the first Passover celebrates the miracle, and one recites the Hallel as giving thanks. But on the second one, it is a chance to make it up, not a celebration of what happened earlier. Surely, they say the Hallel while bringing the sacrifice on both occasions.</p><p>The <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2021/02/pesachim-75.html" target="_blank">cooking instructions</a> on the second Passover are the same: the meat is roasted and is eaten with matzah and better herbs. Here too, the sacrifice is brought even on Shabbat.</p><p>Art: The Basket of Bread by Salvador Dali</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/96.txt
<a id="src-00459"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/96.txt`

Pesachim 96 - The very first Seder
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj08vWYfHyQEGWu3jdP-5MgkJu3uJkwm1C7czoPqCHNx3Kd_j18sWcqz10a8h0JxDUNdmKf9rJ3jzW2OidaD2rLB8tBwfJznPFrnMpLB0BEzQeuguXcsE3trP0NAknkxIghPdZfptj7twM0/s560/sheep-and-chickens-in-a-barn-eugene-verboeckhoven.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="400" data-original-width="560" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj08vWYfHyQEGWu3jdP-5MgkJu3uJkwm1C7czoPqCHNx3Kd_j18sWcqz10a8h0JxDUNdmKf9rJ3jzW2OidaD2rLB8tBwfJznPFrnMpLB0BEzQeuguXcsE3trP0NAknkxIghPdZfptj7twM0/s320/sheep-and-chickens-in-a-barn-eugene-verboeckhoven.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The very first Seder happened in Egypt on the eve of the Exodus. How was it different from the Seder that occurred every subsequent year?<p></p><p>First, one had to designate the sheep to be eaten at the Seder early, <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1820" target="_blank">three days in advance</a>. There was a special procedure of <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1830" target="_blank">sprinkling its blood</a> on the lintel and the two doorposts using a hyssop bundle. In Egypt, this was to distinguish between the Jewish homes and the Egyptian homes, which would not apply to subsequent years.</p><p>The first Seder was conducted <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1828" target="_blank">in haste, dressed and ready to go</a>. Anybody who has been at the Seder nowadays knows that "whoever prolongs it is praiseworthy."</p><p>Art:&nbsp;Sheep and chickens in a barn&nbsp; Eugene Verboeckhoven</p>

---

### content/pesachim/97.txt
<a id="src-00460"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/97.txt`

Pesachim 97 - The sheep goes to graze
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh43LMxjLX7Gsqc7R3JaP3If22qM1Z0q28wkyCK0h9MIA2znC8pVOqrKKc9joeCYA1eDZ5RyiE-7WMJvGX-I225LeO56WNbiPR6W3OrXfwSu3wstCWwYtwQiJ55dRa4i5GeQIReZ0CWxEwu/s1640/sheep.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="940" data-original-width="1640" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh43LMxjLX7Gsqc7R3JaP3If22qM1Z0q28wkyCK0h9MIA2znC8pVOqrKKc9joeCYA1eDZ5RyiE-7WMJvGX-I225LeO56WNbiPR6W3OrXfwSu3wstCWwYtwQiJ55dRa4i5GeQIReZ0CWxEwu/s320/sheep.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The Passover offering slaughtered for the Seder must be a <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=12#P1822" target="_blank">male animal, a sheep or a goat, in its first year</a>. What happens when one designates a female animal or a male that is older than a year? The animal is a sacrifice but is not a fit for its designated purpose. Therefore, it is sent to graze in the pasture until it gets a blemish. Then it is sold, and the money is used to buy a replacement, which the owner then brings as a peace offering.<p></p><p>What if someone designated a lamb and then died? The offering goes as an inheritance to his son. If the son was not registered to eat this offering, he cannot eat it this year, but he also cannot eat it the next year because by then, the lamb will be over a year old! Therefore, the son will later bring this animal as a peace offering.</p><p>Art: Grazing sheep by Carleton Wiggins</p><p><br /></p>

---

### content/pesachim/98.txt
<a id="src-00461"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/98.txt`

Pesachim 98 - A lost sheep
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhLuY9jPB9JAF13XEarCRcpEwwPhHx4GbT-nqIjnJF5ngscBSukZFyv6hCl0_CvmIREqQ41yg_eErfPXSmdzEVMVv9PWYBq_FxdDBcvYr6Tvtf0M9VAQu3PJc-P-7GbwTXBAex0EGwtJXFV/s1280/sheep.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="774" data-original-width="1280" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhLuY9jPB9JAF13XEarCRcpEwwPhHx4GbT-nqIjnJF5ngscBSukZFyv6hCl0_CvmIREqQ41yg_eErfPXSmdzEVMVv9PWYBq_FxdDBcvYr6Tvtf0M9VAQu3PJc-P-7GbwTXBAex0EGwtJXFV/s320/sheep.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>If one's Passover sheep became intermingled with offerings of other types (such as guilt-offering and burnt-offering), we now have a problem. Since different offerings have different laws, we cannot bring any of the animals because we don't know which is which. The solution? - Let them all graze until they develop a blemish, and sell them, and use that money to buy each type of sacrifice in the mix. Each new sacrifice must cost as much as the most expensive one in the original mix.<p></p><p>Another problem: a group of people lost their Passover sheep. They made one of them a messenger to find it. He found it and slaughtered it for them. But they, being afraid that he won't find the animal, got another one and slaughtered it. Which one do they eat now?</p><p>The answer: if he slaughtered his first, then it is the group's offering, and all eat from it. If they slaughtered theirs first, they eat the new one, but the messenger eats the original one because he slaughtered it for himself. What if they do not know which one was slaughtered first? He still eats his, but they cannot eat any because they do not know which one is theirs. However, since one of the two is definitely theirs - it's just that they don't know which - they fulfilled the mitzvah and do not bring it on Second Passover.</p><p>Now there is a whole group of attempts to rectify this situation by making all kinds of conditions, but none works in all life situations. The conclusion is that it is better to be silent and not fix it with all kinds of clauses.</p><p>Art: A shepherd with his flock by Anton Mauve</p><div><br /></div>

---

### content/pesachim/99.txt
<a id="src-00462"></a>

**Source file:** `content/pesachim/99.txt`

Pesachim 99 - No eating till evening
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQLlgnAKerrz7fQL355LrGKMUD8TVMUMbNF0Usi3PQ-4Z-zeedh_vPkJot_Ya8gTIKHFL0VhqMQexP5IHmfmVmYLXo6k9lLUgbVznTw9_jaVV8l0wkKfLSyEcBKOD_PYxk3f9IPeR2VdaE/s638/Philippe_Mercier_-_Le_jeune_Degustateur.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="461" data-original-width="638" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgQLlgnAKerrz7fQL355LrGKMUD8TVMUMbNF0Usi3PQ-4Z-zeedh_vPkJot_Ya8gTIKHFL0VhqMQexP5IHmfmVmYLXo6k9lLUgbVznTw9_jaVV8l0wkKfLSyEcBKOD_PYxk3f9IPeR2VdaE/s320/Philippe_Mercier_-_Le_jeune_Degustateur.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>In the afternoon before the Seder, one should not eat until night (and Seder) comes. What is the purpose of this rule? He cannot eat anything anyway! If it is chametz that he wants to eat, it is already prohibited in the second half-day before Passover. And if it is matzah, then it is already prohibited because one should not eat matzah the day before Seder - to welcome its taste at the Seder. Guess? The answer is that one should not eat egg matzah (called rich matzah) or too many vegetables.&nbsp;<p></p><p>Even the poorest among the Jews should eat while reclining, imitating rich and free people. Some say that he should recline during the first two wine cups while discussing being a slave, and some - that he should recline during the last two wine cups while discussing becoming free. To fulfill both views, he reclines for all four cups.</p><p>All should have four cups of wine. Even the poorest person supplied with the communal charity has to be provided with four cups of wine.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;&nbsp;Young Wine Taster by Philippe Mercier</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/10.txt
<a id="src-00463"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/10.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 10 – The New Year of trees
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhytu4Kd4Y1p7pETR4pi2XqkCadWxPLccMRI-dsS3wEXiWe0odAAx5yr45r_ZFtHkypchOfb2zfxT4ksFTYbPVvGVbr9gpelqhBS8E1xE2zGDfvwsZ54zwK457cFMP2dcrHYjnZrSXG1ldK/s1600/Landscape+with+Oak+Trees+By+Caspar+David+Friedrich.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="230" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhytu4Kd4Y1p7pETR4pi2XqkCadWxPLccMRI-dsS3wEXiWe0odAAx5yr45r_ZFtHkypchOfb2zfxT4ksFTYbPVvGVbr9gpelqhBS8E1xE2zGDfvwsZ54zwK457cFMP2dcrHYjnZrSXG1ldK/s1600/Landscape+with+Oak+Trees+By+Caspar+David+Friedrich.jpg" width="320" /></a>The years of a tree are also counted from the first of Tishrei. Why is it important to know how old a tree is? – Because for the first three years, the fruit of the tree is called "orlah" and cannot be eaten, so we need to know when to count the first year. As it turns out if the tree is planted at least 30 days before Rosh Hashanah, this is already considered the first full year of its life. Even so, after the third Rosh Hashanah, the fruit is not permitted immediately, but only after the fifteenth of Shvat, also known as "Tu B'Shvat."
<br />
<br />
From the rule above, we see that thirty days in a year a considered an entire year. However, this is only the opinion of Rabbi Elazar. By contrast, Rabbi Meir says that even one day in a year is already considered an entire year. If so, how does Rabbi Meir explains the rule of thirty days for orlah cited above? He says that the tree indeed needs thirty days to take root, but if not for that, even one day in a year would make it a year old.
<br />
<br />
We can see that these teachers agree on the month the world was created and place it in Nisan. How? – We will see this on the next page.
<br />
<br />
Art: Landscape with Oak Trees By Caspar David Friedrich, 1811

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/11.txt
<a id="src-00464"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/11.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 11 - When was the world created?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_HR3gpKJEaxSKsLjQsDkxNR7AWNvVk96fAkDi3CLMi7bQgpHkiUxDV2juvXEXqVV1jCBb621fmIcQJR4NX2pcxg_4gMn386lfHbtnRNsz_YSzYKRzIKPNb2Fe73npszkmu8i8RL9jXWLn/s1000/alfred-sisley-country-spring-under-fruit-trees.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="834" data-original-width="1000" height="267" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi_HR3gpKJEaxSKsLjQsDkxNR7AWNvVk96fAkDi3CLMi7bQgpHkiUxDV2juvXEXqVV1jCBb621fmIcQJR4NX2pcxg_4gMn386lfHbtnRNsz_YSzYKRzIKPNb2Fe73npszkmu8i8RL9jXWLn/s320/alfred-sisley-country-spring-under-fruit-trees.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The Holiday of Rosh Hashanah, or New Year, <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=23#P3424" target="_blank">is celebrated on the first day of the seventh month</a>. It is the day of judgment and introspection and also of the blowing of the shofar. This day also marks the creation of the world and of mankind. That is the opinion of Rabbi Eliezer. What is his proof? "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=1#P11" target="_blank">God said, 'The earth shall send forth vegetation.</a>" This suggests that the land of covered with mature vegetation. Which month is that? It is the fall month of Tishrei.<p></p><p>Rabbi Yehoshuah interprets the same verse differently. "Earth send forth vegetation" means the land that is only beginning to bring forth vegetation, and this is the spring month of Nisan. So in his opinion, the world was created in Nisan.</p><p>Rabbi Eliezer places other events also in Tishrei. This month, Abraham and Jacob were born, Sarah, Rachel, and Hannah were remembered, and Joseph went out of the Egyptian prison. The text of Rosh Hashanah's prayers accepted today follows the opinion of Rabbi Eliezer.</p><p>Art: Country Spring by Alfred Sisley</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/12.txt
<a id="src-00465"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/12.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 12 - The laws of vegetables
<p><a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/05/rosh-hashanah-2-four-new-years.html" target="_blank"></a></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUVZ2Yn-obkeuWWITHMDE9ybL68AjYhNkpOhG6A1UuIXydu8zoJOGZE6mW_TlOURYViO_ABUdAZrwjnROwO6NIgsaNPRiN6RmQfGCSXjuucIuv0y9-QXABrwcOvM3ZqP5oKjZywqgqMmXs/s890/Vegetable-Seller-Joachim-Beuckelaer.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="664" data-original-width="890" height="239" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhUVZ2Yn-obkeuWWITHMDE9ybL68AjYhNkpOhG6A1UuIXydu8zoJOGZE6mW_TlOURYViO_ABUdAZrwjnROwO6NIgsaNPRiN6RmQfGCSXjuucIuv0y9-QXABrwcOvM3ZqP5oKjZywqgqMmXs/s320/Vegetable-Seller-Joachim-Beuckelaer.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>We started this tractate saying that there are four beginnings of the year, and what each one appertains to. There is a new year (Rosh Hashanah) for vegetables, and it falls on the first of the month of Tishrei. What are the laws for vegetables? They relate to tithes.<p></p><p>In general, one has to give tithes of the grain that he collects in the land of Israel. The Sages extended this law to vegetables and obligated one to set aside tithes of vegetables before eating them. The obligation of tithes is year by year. Thus, if one picks a vegetable on the last day before Rosh Hashanah and then another after the sun goes down and it is already a new year, he must give the titles separately. He cannot give a tithe from the vegetables of one year for the next, nor the following year's tithe from this one.</p><p>(Incidentally, he cannot pick vegetables on the Rosh Hashanah day itself, so we assume that we are talking about a non-Jew he did it for him, and even that - on his own accord.)</p><p>Some more laws of the vegetables. The obligation to give tithes starts at the moment when one harvests it from the ground. However, one can still snack from them. Later, when one bundles the produce for the market to sell, one can no longer snack from it until he separates tithes. That is for the vegetables that are sold by bundles. If the vegetables are sold in baskets, the cutoff point for snacks is putting them in a basket.</p><p>Art: Vegetable Seller by Joachim Beuckelaer</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/13.txt
<a id="src-00466"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/13.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 13 - Rosh Hashanah for vows and the question of exact measurements
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjh-T46qCtm4daAUlk15GxBuTrIhCYfFl5Eto6onOp1LaQ_d8PRqKr2u0loKrD_0JHzaR8NY97uVBSi8rlGEwsCrPEi4MVuZUU5mFfAHmEz9lOaX2h_P5_ibqeVS-PPq0n3CcvRQB-i9P5T/s650/A-Basket-of-Grapes-Pierre-Dupuis.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="499" data-original-width="650" height="246" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjh-T46qCtm4daAUlk15GxBuTrIhCYfFl5Eto6onOp1LaQ_d8PRqKr2u0loKrD_0JHzaR8NY97uVBSi8rlGEwsCrPEi4MVuZUU5mFfAHmEz9lOaX2h_P5_ibqeVS-PPq0n3CcvRQB-i9P5T/s320/A-Basket-of-Grapes-Pierre-Dupuis.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Rosh Hashanah for vows also stars on the first of the month of Tishrei. But what does this mean? Imagine that one has taken a vow which prohibits her any benefit from a particular fellow. Then she should observe it for a year, until the same month and the exact date come next year. However, if she vowed "this year," then she should not derive benefit from her friend until the first of Tishrei next year. This is true even if only one day is left before the first of Tishrei. Even those people who say that one day in a year cannot be counted a year - here they will agree to one day. That is because our vower intended to cause herself some suffering, which she has achieved even in one day.<div><br /></div><div>The Talmud now goes back to the discussion of tithes. The natural place for this discussion is in the <a href="https://www.sefaria.org/Mishnah_Maaser_Sheni" target="_blank">Mishnah Maaser</a>. However, the Babylonian Talmud discusses the laws of Israeli produce only incidentally.</div><div><br /></div><div>Grain and grapes are obligated in tithes once they grow one-third of their total growth. But did the Sages know when this happened? And in general, do we need to be so meticulous? Here the answer is yes. Otherwise, these measures would make little sense. A mikvah must have at least forty se'ah of water; the amount of food to transmit ritual impurity is the size of an egg, and so on.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art:&nbsp;A Basket of Grapes by Pierre Dupuis</div><div><br /></div>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/14.txt
<a id="src-00467"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/14.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 14 - Tu Bishvat
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDxERazhI6wm8pJcGjcQuv1covz1s0GNo70NqNEnlUd7LuQguN4IuagYXjvQ2CWXgil9Sq2VrM6s-fDW95tLMZGqEh8pfsCW60iS7o3kqtnJdCpbcxYkdybYL-kN-xSncGftXEiu6iJXoE/s600/the-large-tree-1889.jpg%2521Large.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="600" data-original-width="447" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiDxERazhI6wm8pJcGjcQuv1covz1s0GNo70NqNEnlUd7LuQguN4IuagYXjvQ2CWXgil9Sq2VrM6s-fDW95tLMZGqEh8pfsCW60iS7o3kqtnJdCpbcxYkdybYL-kN-xSncGftXEiu6iJXoE/s320/the-large-tree-1889.jpg%2521Large.jpg" width="238" /></a></div><br />Tu Bishvat, the 15th of the month of Shvat, marks the New Year of the trees. Why is this day significant in the life of a tree? Because by then, most of the rainy days of the season have passed. In Israel, rain does not fall throughout the year but only during the rainy season, from mid-autumn through winter. These rains cause sap to rise in the trees, and the new fruits of the tree are ready to emerge.<p></p><p>But wait! Didn't we say that the <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/05/rosh-hashanah-10-new-year-of-trees.html" target="_blank">New Year of the trees is on the first of Tishrei</a>? Yes, and yet there is no contradiction. The Tishrei New Year is to count the number of years in the life of a tree. For the first three years, the tree is "orlah," and its fruit cannot be used. In the fourth, its fruit is taken to Jerusalem and eaten there.</p><p>By contrast, Tu Bishvat is for separating tithes. In different years, there are different kinds of tithes. There is tithe for the poor and tithe to be eaten in Jerusalem. Tu Bishvat serves as a demarkation telling the year the fruit belongs and therefore the tithe that should be taken from it.</p><p>Art:&nbsp;The Large Tree by Paul Gauguin</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/15.txt
<a id="src-00468"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/15.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 15 - Etrog - a tree or a vegetable?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjWYjINgK5wgNxRzdmXZFXFE1rrQU86Oxd7vKR0anu1VEaRkzGTInvF318ioGXhrRUhRdfv1823-ISSe7ZEIICyHgPh_xstECA-yuO3YqxSQFjk94RCXaF3XO_TVtsMbxAJlmVdPZN7Rea5/s750/the-lemon.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="472" data-original-width="750" height="201" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjWYjINgK5wgNxRzdmXZFXFE1rrQU86Oxd7vKR0anu1VEaRkzGTInvF318ioGXhrRUhRdfv1823-ISSe7ZEIICyHgPh_xstECA-yuO3YqxSQFjk94RCXaF3XO_TVtsMbxAJlmVdPZN7Rea5/s320/the-lemon.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>The <a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/03/sukkah-35-etrog-or-citron.html" target="_blank">etrog</a> is similar to a tree in three ways, and it is similar to a vegetable in one way. The etrog is treated as a tree fruit for the laws of <i>orlah</i>: for the first three years, the fruit of any tree in Israel cannot be eaten or even used. For the laws of <i>revai</i>: in the fourth year, the fruit is taken to Jerusalem and eaten there. For the laws of shmita: the fruits of the seventh year are free for all.<p></p><p>However, the etrog is like a vegetable for the laws of tithing. That is, the tithing obligation begins at the moment when it is picked. That is because, as a vegetable, the etrog keeps absorbing water and uses it for growth all the time until it is harvested. This opinion is not unanimous, and there were different practices regarding the etrog. For Rabbi Akiva, this was a practical issue. Once, he separated the tithes two times, according to two different opinions. The Talmud discusses whose opinions these were and what did his actions mean.</p><p>Art: The lemon by Edouard Manet</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/16.txt
<a id="src-00469"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/16.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 16 - When is judgement?
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiof5WPF-25145MyQ8KIyRV1DLP1CRfyBybe_7Wm0x9zM9GM6TUdL9MgZ-bncR-iI6NkY9fy7RCv3mfbavprwj16Ye6iJmOCVg6Wvexn5gh6Xok3FPoPJs-t6Dr5KFqEAc6cdBDcHYRnXNV/s1024/flinck_verstoting_hagar_grt.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="807" data-original-width="1024" height="252" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiof5WPF-25145MyQ8KIyRV1DLP1CRfyBybe_7Wm0x9zM9GM6TUdL9MgZ-bncR-iI6NkY9fy7RCv3mfbavprwj16Ye6iJmOCVg6Wvexn5gh6Xok3FPoPJs-t6Dr5KFqEAc6cdBDcHYRnXNV/s320/flinck_verstoting_hagar_grt.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>There are four periods of judgment. On Passover, the world is judged for grain. On Shavuot, it is judged regarding the fruit of the tree. On Rosh Hashanah, all who come into this world pass before Him, following the phrase "<a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt2633.htm" target="_blank">He that fashions their hearts, understands their deeds</a>." The reason for knowing the times of judgment is to pray with particular intensity and purpose.<p></p><p>However, there are other opinions: man is judged every day, man is judged every hour, and so on. Many questions come up regarding free will, the efficacy of prayer for the sick if their fate was already decided, and so on.</p><p>There are some rules that Rabbi Yitzhak related. A person is judged according to his situation at the moment and not his future deeds. Source? Ishmael was saved in the desert <a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=21#P531" target="_blank">because of his current plight</a>, regardless of his future evil deeds.</p><p>Further, when one calls for judgement for his fellow, he attracts undue attention to his own sins. Sources: Sarah said, "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=16#P387" target="_blank">Let God judge between&nbsp;me and you</a>." Next, "<a href="https://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=23#P574" target="_blank">And Abraham came to eulogize Sarah and weep for her</a>."</p><p>Art: The Dismissal of Hagar by Govert Flinck&nbsp;</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/17.txt
<a id="src-00470"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/17.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 17 - Tolerance
<p></p><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikoOODjDWyHMbazedj5XOmiZ2Wn-6LUzQTJML3Eh6lVOUznhVZ1viyPqQJtaJV3-_PUypZHdpJF3vaC1az_RgiUO_AGBn74Qk-yMZM_5PwFfISktOTYMeAWLSpsCpepuvmC8E2DXaLl91m/s540/three-books.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="326" data-original-width="540" height="193" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEikoOODjDWyHMbazedj5XOmiZ2Wn-6LUzQTJML3Eh6lVOUznhVZ1viyPqQJtaJV3-_PUypZHdpJF3vaC1az_RgiUO_AGBn74Qk-yMZM_5PwFfISktOTYMeAWLSpsCpepuvmC8E2DXaLl91m/s320/three-books.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>There are three books open on Rosh Hashanah: the wicked, the righteous, and the intermediate. The righteous are written and sealed in the book of righteous, for life. The wicked are written and sealed in the book of the wicked, for death. The intermediate people are given ten days until Yom Kippur to improve themselves. If they succeed, they are written for life and if not - for death.<p></p><p>This passage conceals more than it tells. There are at least four ways to understand it. That "life" and "death" refer to the spiritual state in the World to Come. That the terms "righteous" and "wicked" do not refer to what is commonly called "good" and "bad" deeds; instead, the measure of good and bad deeds is unknown to us and is unexpected. The third approach says that "life" and "death" mean that the lifespan is expanded or shortened. Another approach is that "righteous" is a person whose merits outweigh his evil deeds.&nbsp;</p><p>Notwithstanding, one who does not insist on his rights, and drops the entire matter when being offended - such a person deserves that in judgment, his bad deeds are also dropped. What is the source for that? "<a href="https://www.mechon-mamre.org/p/pt/pt1807.htm" target="_blank">He (God) pardons transgression and overlooks sin</a>." The Talmud reads this as follows: "Whose transgression does He pardon? - One who overlooks sins committed against himself."</p><p>Art: Still life with three books by Van Gogh</p>

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/18.txt
<a id="src-00471"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/18.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 18 – Sometimes sorrow, sometimes joy
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwJEs_2E29Ivikyhj1I6n8-E9kGXhXDH0bQqNAUd2b2Viyvcr9gnSt13Lb8OgTxIOvX529mkppPKrnWG2C2mxK4YntR3SuPYZvKA5gg4FeuuBNmv6aG136LhujyBM0G6_sKjZgkvCkvwDn/s640/Herp+van+Willem.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="430" data-original-width="640" height="215" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwJEs_2E29Ivikyhj1I6n8-E9kGXhXDH0bQqNAUd2b2Viyvcr9gnSt13Lb8OgTxIOvX529mkppPKrnWG2C2mxK4YntR3SuPYZvKA5gg4FeuuBNmv6aG136LhujyBM0G6_sKjZgkvCkvwDn/s320/Herp+van+Willem.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Initially, the Court would determine the New Month according to the sighting of the moon.&nbsp; They would then send messengers to far-away provinces to announce when the Holidays of Passover, Rosh Hashanah, Chanukah, and Purim will be.
<br />
<br />
However, the above list omits the fast days in Tammuz and Tevet, why is that? – Because in the times of the Temple these days were observed not as fasts but as days of feasts and happiness. Still, since the prophets knew that the Second Temple will also be destroyed, they did not abrogate the fast days for good. 
<br />
<br />
In fact, so many miraculous salvations happened in the days of the Second Temple that the Sages had to write down a scroll enumerating these minor festivals when fasting and eulogizing the dead were not allowed. It was called “The Scroll of Fasts.” Later, with the destruction of the Second Temple, these minor festivals were also canceled. Some say that they stayed since they were not related to the Temple. All agree that the amount of trouble and suffering magnified in the subsequent generations, and people became numb to them. Hence, they did not appreciate the deliverance from them either.
<br />
<br />
Art: Interior With A Family Feasting And Dancing by Willem van, the Elder Herp, c. 1637

---

### content/rosh_hashanah/19.txt
<a id="src-00472"></a>

**Source file:** `content/rosh_hashanah/19.txt`

Rosh Hashanah 19 - The court sets the time
<a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/05/rosh-hashanah-18-sometimes-sorrow.html" target="_blank"></a><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/05/rosh-hashanah-18-sometimes-sorrow.html" target="_blank"></a><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm6ahz5qA3SrUrrtG225_1UzoQZuAMzUUsdtSGGdUrzXj4cq3bXyQIRRs8SDF3UJZ50wG29mUrEgAFJNsUpA3T-6EXGw-Kj5gIzpm9Ibtps8jFSvYQGv1AfbI4gOv3pGS9J7CXvz23OtfO/s700/andrew-wyeth--crescent-moon.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="700" data-original-width="500" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm6ahz5qA3SrUrrtG225_1UzoQZuAMzUUsdtSGGdUrzXj4cq3bXyQIRRs8SDF3UJZ50wG29mUrEgAFJNsUpA3T-6EXGw-Kj5gIzpm9Ibtps8jFSvYQGv1AfbI4gOv3pGS9J7CXvz23OtfO/s320/andrew-wyeth--crescent-moon.jpg" width="229" /></a></div><a href="https://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2014/05/rosh-hashanah-18-sometimes-sorrow.html" target="_blank">As we learned earlier</a>, once the court (Sanhedrin) confirms the New Moon, the day becomes the first day of the month (Rosh Chodesh.) The calendar for Shabbat is different. Shabbat comes on the seventh day, and the court has no power to accelerate or delay this. By contrast, the first of the following month comes either twenty-nine or thirty days after the previous. Depending on the court's determination, the exact date for every Holiday, such as Rosh Hashanah and Passover, may change. This setting of the date will affect the dates when people can or cannot do work. It will also affect the dates when they can or cannot eat chametz and should eat matzah.<div><br /></div><div>Therefore, the court would send messengers who would travel to distant lands such as Babylonia and inform the Jewish community about the date when the New Moon was declared. There were a total of six months when this knowledge was necessary. One of them was Elul - because of Rosh Hashanah that followed that month. The other was the month of Tishrei - because of Yom Kippur on the tenth day of Tishrei. Why did they have to trouble the messengers two months in a row, seeing that the month of Elul was almost always twenty-nine days, and thus the month could be calculated directly? In setting the next month, the court took the needs of the whole nation into account. Therefore, they could make the Elul month complete thirty days and delay Rosh Hashanah on rare occasions.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Crescent Moon by Andrew Wyeth</div><div><br /></div><div><br /></div>
